The Governor-General's Speech Contained Insulting Intent

Obstacles to Administrative and Legislative Cooperation

Reuters, Manila, 16th: When the Philippine Legislative Council held its opening ceremony today, Governor-General Davis gave a long speech, advising the Legislative Council to stop empty talk and carry out real construction work. Important members of both houses were dissatisfied, believing that it contained insulting intent and fearing that administrative and legislative cooperation would be impossible from now on.

Earthquake in the Republic of Ecuador

Latacunga City Completely Destroyed

National News Agency, Quito (Ecuador), 16th: Latacunga in South American Ecuador was destroyed by an earthquake at 3 pm today. It is one of the important cities in Ecuador, with a population of 15,000. It is located sixty miles due south of here. The details of the damage are unknown due to traffic obstruction, but it is expected that there will be many casualties. According to those who have taken refuge here, the earthquake has not yet completely stopped. A relief team is being rushed here to rescue.

Commentary

A Retrospect and Prospect of the Pacific International Academic Society (6) (Continued) - Bin

Although there is no absolute advantage or disadvantage in all international organizations, it depends on the efforts of the people of each country and the participating representatives. Our country has not gained any practical benefits from joining the League of Nations, but we should not give up eating because of choking because it is useless to us and then declare withdrawal. The success or failure of diplomacy does not lie in empty arguments, nor in the sympathy of a few people abroad, nor in whether to participate in international organizations, but entirely in the actual efforts of the country. Moreover, the Pacific International Academic Society cannot have any resolutions, let alone the power to execute them. Its ability to resolve international disputes is only to make suggestions. If our people regard the society as a tool for international liaison, it can be regarded as a living Buddha who helps the poor and relieves the needy, but it cannot be hoped for too much, otherwise the more hope there is, the greater the disappointment will be. If our people and our representatives can take a dim view of it, they can regard the society as an academic group, or they can regard the representatives of various countries attending our country this time as a travel experience, or they can vigorously oppose it, which seems unnecessary. Moreover, the venue of this meeting was decided at the Xijing meeting two years ago. Our representatives should have recognized the Chinese Pacific International Academic Society and formally notified various countries, making it difficult to stop. If we go back on our word temporarily, it will be more deeply related to our national dignity, which is what we cannot but carefully consider. Although the so-called taking a dim view is by no means perfunctory and sloppy, we should not have any extravagant hopes for the society, but we still cannot relax in the slightest for this conference. We should clearly understand the situation of the first, second, and third conferences and learn from the lessons of the past. On the one hand, we should have a detailed setup of the venue to fulfill our duty as the host and sincerely treat the guests with affection, which is enough to show our respect for the representatives of various countries. On the other hand, our people should fully express their legitimate demands for the society before the meeting and should awaken the attention of compatriots throughout the country and oppressed ethnic groups along the Pacific coast to jointly supervise the society and put it on the right track. As for our country's attending representatives, their responsibility is even more important. Before the meeting, they should have sufficient research on various topics. During the discussion, they should make detailed and practical expositions and serious protests on all facts that violate justice and public reason in the Pacific International and all the pain suffered by China under the shackles of unequal treaties so that the representatives of various countries can have a full understanding. On this point, the author has earnestly expressed his wishes in the above article, and here I respectfully express my hope again. Moreover, if the representatives of various countries in this conference can all act as scholars, based on the position of public reason and justice, and conduct a purely objective study of various issues, and promote and supervise their governments to change their policies of foreign aggression and liberate the shackles of weaker ethnic groups to permanently consolidate world peace, then not only will our country be deeply blessed, but also the future of human culture will be realized. That is also the starting point of the society's purpose and the earnest hope of our people.

This article has detailed the current situation of the Pacific and the past of the Pacific International Academic Society. Finally, I respectfully quote Mr. Sun Yat-sen's last words on the Pacific issue to warn the people of the country and to conclude this article.

Mr. Sun Yat-sen said, "In the past, the Mediterranean issue and the Atlantic issue, I can ignore them. However, the Pacific issue from now on is really related to the survival of our Chinese nation and the destiny of the Chinese country. The center of gravity of the Pacific is China. To fight for the sea power of the Pacific is to fight for the right of the Chinese gateway. Whoever holds this gateway has this hall, this treasure. People are fighting for me, how can I ignore it?" May the people and representatives of our country savor this teaching carefully. (End)

Important News

4th Plenary Session of the National Government

Hebei Province's Qingxiang Affairs Approved for a Three-Month Extension

Establishment of Civil Service Screening Committees in Remote Provinces

The National Government held its 4th Plenary Session on the morning of the 17th, attended by committee members Ding Weifen, Ye Chucang, Shao Yuanzhong, Yu Youren, Chen Guofu, Cai Yuanpei, Zhu Peide, Wang Boqun, Wang Zhengting, and Kong Xiangxi Shao Lizi, with Yu Youren presiding. Matters discussed (2) The Executive Yuan submitted a report stating that the Hebei Provincial Government reported that the Qingxiang affairs in the province had been carried out since January 1 of this year, and the six-month period has expired. It is appropriate to follow the order to end it. However, Hebei has a special local situation and the banditry has not been suppressed. It is proposed to request a special extension of three months to facilitate further progress to complete the main government affairs. Accordingly, the document has been submitted to be transferred for review and approval. The resolution was approved. (2) The Examination Yuan submitted a report proposing to establish preliminary review committees for civil service screening in remote provinces in order to end the screening affairs as soon as possible. Drafted regulations were submitted for review and promulgation. The resolution was amended, approved, and promulgated. (3) The resolution to promulgate the organizational regulations of the International Trade Bureau of the Ministry of Industry. (4) The resolution to appoint Nan Guixin as a member of the Huai River Guidance Committee. (5) The resolution to approve the resignation of Pan Xulun, a staff member of the Accounting Office concurrently serving as Deputy Director of the Accounting Bureau. Zhao Dihua will succeed in all the vacated positions. (6) The resolution to appoint Wu Han as the Chief of Staff of the Guard Army. (7) The resolution to approve the resignation of Yu Jifu, a technician of the Construction Committee. Wang Chongzhi was appointed as the technician of the committee.

Suppression of Communist Troops and Capture of Guangchang

Liu Ruiheng Arrives in Jiangxi to Inspect the Military Medical Situation

Luo's Division Establishes Contact with Ma's Brigade in Ganzhou

Nanchang Correspondence: Guangchang is located south of Nanfeng, east of Ningdu, and north of Shicheng, bordering Jianning and Ninghua in Fujian. It is an important place for Jiangnan to connect with Fujian. A few days ago, after the suppression of communist troops captured Lichuan, the eastern Jiangxi communist bandits, except for a part that fled to Fujian, mostly retreated to Guangchang, planning to unite with the western Fujian communist bandits. Then the suppressing communist troops bravely advanced and captured the important passes of Kangdu, Qianshan, and Kuzhu on the 11th, and immediately took the Guangchang city with a left and right encirclement formation. At noon on the 12th, our troops had occupied Datangxu and Shunhua Wu on the opposite bank of Guangcheng and fiercely fired at the bandits in the city. Another part of our troops attacked Xinpo to cut off the communist bandits' westward retreat, and another part circled around Guangchang to the south for dozens of miles to Baishui Town to cut off the connection between the Guangchang communist bandits and the Shicheng communist bandits. Until today, the aircraft reported that the suppressing communist troops had already captured Guangchang.

In recent days, the battles in Guangchang, Ningdu, Donggu, and other places have been extremely fierce. All the rear military doctors have set off to the front line to rescue the wounded soldiers. Liu Hengrui, the Director-General of Military Medical Services, came to Jiangxi from Beijing to inspect the military medical situation. On the 12th, he arrived in the province and convened a meeting of military medical cadres at the Maternity and Child Hospital on the 14th. Jiang Kezong, the Director of the Military Medical Department, Liu Dalian, the Director of the Military Station Health Department, the directors of the military medical departments in the province, the directors of the rear hospitals, the directors of the field hospitals, and many foreign consultants attended the meeting and resolved many issues such as battlefield rescue, military hygiene, and surgical treatment of wounded soldiers. As for the surgical teams and military doctors dispatched by the headquarters from Beijing to Jiangxi, they have all been transferred to the front line to work. The General Headquarters received a telegram from Commander-in-Chief He yesterday saying that thousands of guerrillas and prisoners will be escorted to Nanchang in the next few days and handed over to the Road Bureau and the Transportation Department to be compiled into labor teams to engage in road construction under strict supervision, and personnel will be sent from the Training Department of the General Headquarters to train them. The right-wing force of the suppressing communist troops is also progressing rapidly. After Luo Lin's division captured Suichuan, the bandits of Hu, Luo, Zeng, and Liu fled in all directions. Luo's division beheaded and captured many scattered bandits and established contact with Ma's brigade in Ganzhou. Li Mingrui's troops fled to southern Jiangxi. The fellow villagers of the Jiangnan brigade specially elected Chen Panzao to go to Ji'an to petition Commander-in-Chief Chen to send troops to suppress them. However, the Chen's troops originally assigned to attack the front of Donggu have arrived near Donggu, so the Ganzhou communist bandits specially assigned Ma's brigade to be responsible for the suppression (July 16).

The Tragic Situation of Overseas Chinese in Wonsan During the Korean Riot

Eleven Died and Eighteen Seriously Injured

More Than Two Thousand People Sought Refuge at the Consulate

Also Affected Areas Include Kangwon, Tongchon, and Other Places

Wonsan, Korea Correspondence: Japanese imperialists secretly instigated the Korean people to launch an anti-Chinese movement as a backing for the Wanbaoshan Incident. Therefore, all of Korea, except for the areas bordering China, was affected. Riots began in Wonsan on the evening of the 4th, attacking more than ten stores such as the Yuchenxiang store in Shangdong. It became more intense on the 5th. At 2 pm, Vice Consul Hu and Mr. Xu went to Ge Ma to rescue farmers and workers.

Page 10

All places gathered hundreds of Koreans preparing to seek revenge on the Chinese. Therefore, this trip of Hu and others was very dangerous. After 6 pm, the rioters in various places became more numerous, gathering about thousands of people, beating overseas Chinese and attacking stores everywhere. Dozens of stores were destroyed one after another. Eleven farmers and workers were beaten to death, two of whom have been buried. The remaining corpses were either privately buried or thrown into the river and their whereabouts are still unknown. Eighteen people were seriously injured and have been treated by doctors hired by the Chamber of Commerce. The number of minor injuries is countless. In addition, there are still many people whose life or death is unknown. The police only superficially perfunctorily and failed to stop the chaos, causing the whole city to fall into great chaos. Overseas Chinese fled to the consulate. On the 5th, 6th, and 7th, a total of 1198 men and 287 women were received. On the 8th, 604 men and 7 women were received. On the 9th, 12 men were received. In total, 2108 people were counted. Together with the original residents of Chinatown, there were a total of 2555 people, who were living in the Chinese Association Hall, the Party Headquarters, the Overseas Chinese School, the Chengji warehouse, the homes of the overseas Chinese in Chinatown, and the empty houses of the battalion. The Chamber of Commerce temporarily took on the responsibility of providing food and drink. After the 7th, the Koreans had slightly realized and stopped the riots, but the Japanese still did not allow the Chinese to leave Chinatown. It was not until the morning of the 10th that the local refugees were allowed to return to work first. It is heard that the Wonsan Consulate plans to first request the police station to provide a safety guarantee before allowing the refugees to resume their business. Negotiations are still underway. The overseas Chinese in Changjeon Port, Kangwon Province, were also expelled on the 6th. Four died and seven were seriously injured when they arrived in Wonsan on the 7th. After being beaten and injured, these seven people were buried in the ditch by the Koreans. Fortunately, they were discovered by the store clerk and rescued. They are now being treated in Wonsan and their lives are still in danger. Two Chinese workers were also beaten to death in Paechon-ri, Tongchon County, and the eyeballs of two others were taken out and thrown on the riverbank. Extremely large riots also occurred in other places such as Seopo, Naeho, Hamheung, and Sinpo. The losses of overseas Chinese are incalculable. The Consulate is currently conducting an investigation.

The Japanese side originally wanted to take the opportunity to expel the Chinese workers. At 7 pm on the 8th, the Tongchon Police Station had expelled 555 Chinese railway workers in the county to Wonsan. Others were being sent along the way. The Wonsan Consulate immediately telegraphed the Consul-General to protest to the Governor-General's Office. The Governor-General's Office had no excuse and had to order all places to prohibit expulsion. As a result, more than 300 people who were being sent halfway were left in Tongchon and stopped moving forward (July 10).

The Wanbaoshan Incident

Sino-Japanese Negotiation Documents (4)

Letter from Japanese Consul to Municipal Office:

Regarding the Three-Family Fort Farm issue, we have met numerous times, but there has been no sign of a satisfactory resolution, which I deeply regret. The normally harmonious relationship between the Chinese and Japanese in the local area has been overshadowed by dark clouds since the incident occurred, which is truly concerning. I am constantly anxious about finding a satisfactory compromise. In our previous meeting, the main obstacle to the case was the opposition of the local people. I earnestly requested that your Director use his best efforts to persuade them to desist. I have now received your letter No. 161 of the 14th of this month, and I am aware that you have summoned representatives of the local people to persuade them to desist, but without success. However, if they were informed of the facts and earnestly persuaded, they might be dissuaded. Furthermore, regarding the paddy field project, we will instruct the Koreans to make every effort to avoid anything that is detrimental or inconvenient to the local people, regardless of whether the unexpected damages claimed by the farmers are factual. In short, the implementation of this paddy field project will be a trial run to observe the results before making further plans. I hope you will give it favorable consideration. Furthermore, regarding the dispatch of twelve policemen and the start of construction by Korean farmers mentioned at the end of your letter No. 161 of the 14th of this month, during our previous meeting, I expressed concern that the Korean farmers, being eager to start sowing, might begin construction of the weir without waiting for instructions, thus causing undesirable conflicts with the opposing Chinese farmers. Therefore, on the 12th, I dispatched four plainclothes policemen to the site to specifically restrain the Koreans from acting rashly. This was fully understood by your Director. In other words, the sole purpose of our police dispatch was to restrain the Korean farmers and prevent conflicts with your country's farmers. As for the Korean farmers starting construction, we have not yet received a report of that happening. It may be that the Korean farmers were transporting willow branches, which was mistaken for the start of work. This is merely a preparatory action, as they are currently collecting materials to be used for weir construction after a satisfactory resolution is reached. Please do not misunderstand. Furthermore, if this case is allowed to drag on, it is difficult to guarantee that incidents will not occur, which is not what I desire. We have repeatedly negotiated with you, but you insist on your original position regarding our efforts to reach a satisfactory settlement. Therefore, your side is responsible for any undesirable situation that may arise. I am writing to inform you accordingly.

To: Director Zhou of the Changchun Municipal Preparatory Office

Tashiro Shigetoku, Consul Resident in Changchun

June 16th

Letter from Municipal Office to Japanese Consul:

Upon opening, I have read with respect your Official Document No. 44 of June 16th. The fact that the Korean people of Wanbaoshan forcibly excavated land and dug waterways, intending to build dams across rivers and divert the Itong River, has been determined through joint investigation to be a purely illegal act that violates current laws and lacks a consensual agreement. This infringes upon the legitimate and inherent rights of landowners and farmers. The impact directly and significantly damages the livelihoods of thousands of farmers. The facts are clearly stated in our Official Documents No. 158 of June 11th and No. 161 of June 14th. Any human being with blood and understanding, regardless of nationality, could easily discern the right and wrong with a few words, even the most foolish and ignorant. Based on the results of the joint investigation, the plan to build dams and divert river water is undoubtedly out of the question, and there is no room for further discussion. At this time, the remaining issues to be resolved are only the question of the Korean people's departure and the compensation for damages among the parties involved. The final solution has already been described in our Official Document No. 159 of June 12th. I hope you will carefully consider the options and provide a clear response so that we can conclude this matter as soon as possible. As for the Korean people temporarily staying here, it is certainly acceptable that your side recently dispatched police to convey the intention to stop work. However, now that the intention has been conveyed, you should immediately order them to return. Since we are responsible for protection, we can naturally monitor the cessation of work. There is no need for your side to take superfluous action. Furthermore, we have repeatedly received reports from Changchun County that the Korean people are currently weaving baskets and rolling up blinds with willow branches in preparation for building dams and waterways. Moreover, your police officers seem to be maintaining and promoting this work, which is contrary to the resolution agreed upon by both parties on the 8th of this month. I hope you will investigate this matter, immediately withdraw the personnel, and stop the work in order to avoid further complications. This would be most appreciated.

To: Tashiro, Japanese Consul Resident in Changchun

June 17th (To be continued)

Refugees from Korea Arrive in Qingdao

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Arranges for Their Return to Their Native Places

Refugees Describe the Cruelty of the Koreans

Korean Riot Was Indeed Instigated by the Japanese

Qingdao Dispatch: The Korean massacre of our Chinese residents has aroused national indignation. The Navy recently dispatched the Zhenhai warship to Incheon and other places to escort the refugees back to China. It is reported that several groups of these refugees have returned by ship. About three thousand people disembarked in Yantai. The Qingdao Chamber of Commerce received a telegram from the Yantai Chamber of Commerce on the 14th, stating: "Today, over five hundred refugees returning from Korea will board the Kyodo Maru to Qingdao. We fear that the Qingdao Customs may create difficulties. Please kindly intercede for their release." Another telegram stated: "The previous telegram mentioned that the refugees going to Qingdao need to be transferred to their original residences. We beg you to take care of the transfer and send them off." After receiving the telegrams, the Qingdao Chamber of Commerce immediately notified the Customs Office. Today (the 15th) at noon, the ship finally entered the port. Song Yuting, Chairman of the Chamber of Commerce, and Yu Weiting, Standing Committee Member, personally went to the pier to provide assistance. Dong Zhidao, Section Chief of the Social Affairs Bureau, Ren Dongying, Chief of the Third Branch of the Public Security Bureau, and the Surveillance Section Chief of the Port Authority also arrived to help. The refugees, including men, women, the elderly, and children, numbered about eight hundred. Due to the lack of suitable accommodation, they were temporarily housed in the pier warehouses. The Chamber of Commerce has ordered four hundred catties of steamed buns to feed the refugees. It has also been found that most of these refugees are from Rizhao and Juxian Counties. Therefore, the Qingdao Shipping Association has specially prepared two small steamers, Qingxing and Yusheng, to transport a batch of them to Shijiu, where they will disembark. They are scheduled to depart tonight at six o'clock. The Social Affairs Bureau has notified the Public Security Bureau of Shijiu to send personnel to provide assistance at that time. As for those staying in Qingdao, the Chamber of Commerce has discussed with the Inn Association and arranged for them to be temporarily accommodated in various inns before being sent back to their native places. According to the refugees' representatives, the Korean riot was indeed instigated by the Japanese in secret. Before the outbreak, Japanese police warned the Chinese residents that Koreans would take actions detrimental to the Chinese residents, ordering the Chinese residents not to go out after eight o'clock every night, otherwise they would not be responsible for any danger. Unexpectedly, at ten o'clock on the night of the 2nd of this month, a riot suddenly broke out. The Korean people, each carrying iron bars and iron hooks, were led by the Japanese police to search houses, committing abuse at will. The lightly injured suffered bruises all over their bodies, while the severely injured died immediately. Small children were split in half by their legs. In Pyongyang alone, more than three thousand Chinese residents have died. When the incident occurred, the Japanese police either guided and directed or helped the Koreans to massacre the Chinese residents. There is no doubt that this was a planned and organized act. The representatives said that when they spoke of the Korean cruelty and inhumanity, they lost their voices in grief, and all who heard it were furious. The representatives also said that all Chinese residents with assets and knowledge, and the seriously injured, were prohibited by the Japanese from leaving the country so that outsiders would not understand the truth. Because they were laborers, the Japanese were willing to let them go, but before they left, the Japanese carried out extremely strict inspections, only allowing them to board the ship if they had nothing of value. Their means of oppression were used to the extreme. (July 15th)

Shandong Provincial Government Reports on Refugees Arriving in Shandong

Also Telegraphed Weihai and Yantai to Investigate the Number of Refugees in Detail

Jinan Correspondence: The Shandong Provincial Government, noting that a large number of overseas Chinese have been returning from Korea and landing in Yantai in recent days, and that refugees continue to arrive in Shandong at other ports, sent a special telegram to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs yesterday (the 14th) to report on the situation of the refugees fleeing from Korea to Shandong. It also telegraphed the Yantai and Longkou Public Security Bureaus and the Weihaiwei Administration Office to ascertain the number of refugees fleeing from Korea to Shandong, so as to report to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for future negotiations with Japan. The telegram is transcribed as follows: (1) Telegram to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs in Nanjing: Since the Wanbaoshan incident in Jilin, newspapers have reported increasingly severe Korean riots, and overseas Chinese have been brutally massacred. We have previously telegraphed the National Government to negotiate with the Japanese side to stop the riots and provide relief. Recently, it has been found that a large number of overseas Chinese from Incheon, Wonsan, and other places have fled back to Yantai to seek refuge, and there are also many refugees returning to other coastal ports. This proves that the Korean people are brutal, and the reports in the newspapers are all factual. At the beginning of this incident, the Korean people disregarded public reason and acted violently first. Recently, they have relied on their power to massacre overseas Chinese. This is clearly done under instruction, hence they dare to be so brutal and violent. All citizens share the same indignation. In addition to telegraphing the Yantai and Longkou Public Security Bureaus and the Weihaiwei Administration Office to ascertain the number of people returning to seek refuge, we will further report to your ministry. Your department's efforts to defend against insults and protect the country have their own weight. Please quickly negotiate seriously with the Japanese side and immediately stop the violence to uphold humanity and maintain national rights, and hope to see a reply. Shandong Provincial Government, cold seal. (2) Telegram to the Weihaiwei Administration Office: Telegram to the directors of the Yantai and Longkou Public Security Bureaus: The Korean riots and massacres of our compatriots in the Jilin Wanbaoshan case have been publicized in the newspapers, and we are filled with indignation. We have previously telegraphed the National Government and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to negotiate seriously with the Japanese side to immediately stop the violence, which is on file. Recently, we have heard that there are many refugees returning from Incheon, Wonsan, and other places to the coastal ports of Shandong Province. It is urgent to ascertain the number of people entering the country so as to report it for negotiation. In addition to sending this telegram, we hope you will order an investigation and reply. Shandong Provincial Government, cold seal. (July 15th)

Minister of Foreign Affairs Reports on Diplomacy

The Korean Case and the Wanbaoshan Case Will Be Handled Separately

Telegrams to the U.S. to Investigate the Scope of Suspension of War Debt Payments

Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting hosted a press conference on the 17th to report on the Korean incident and the Wanbaoshan case as follows: (1) The Ministry of Foreign Affairs attaches great importance to the Korean incident. The Japanese government has formally replied, stating that it is making every effort to stop the riot. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs believes that although the riot has subsided, our consulates in Korea had heard about the incident before it occurred and warned the local authorities, requesting them to protect the overseas Chinese with their strength. However, the authorities were unable to stop the riot for several days after it broke out. Our government believes that the Japanese claim to have made every effort to protect the overseas Chinese does not correspond to the facts. We have sent another note to solemnly declare this point and reserve all rights to negotiate damages. (2) Ambassador Wang, stationed in Japan, has arrived in Seoul and is urging the staff of the consulates in Korea to work with the local authorities to conduct a thorough investigation of the losses suffered by the overseas Chinese. After a detailed report arrives in Beijing, we will report it to you. (3) The losses suffered by the overseas Chinese in Korea this time are enormous. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs has remitted over 10,000 yuan to handle relief matters. As for the issue of future compensation, as the amount required is still unknown, it will be decided by the next meeting of the Central Political Council after Ambassador Wang's report. (4) The Ministry of Foreign Affairs believes that responsibility for the Korean case should be clearly defined. Although the Japanese replied that they made every effort to protect the overseas Chinese, this does not correspond to the facts. Therefore, we have sent another note. As for the negotiation of damages, it must wait for Ambassador Wang's report before it can be raised. (5) Although the Wanbaoshan case is related to the Korean case, it will be handled separately because of the different nature of the cases. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs has formulated a solution to the issue of dual nationality of Koreans, which will be discussed when negotiations on the Wanbaoshan case begin.

Minister Wang then reported on the recent diplomatic situation as follows: (1) The treaty between China and Poland came into effect on July 9th. According to international procedures, the documents of ratification should be formally exchanged. It is now scheduled that the representative of Poland, Wei Dentao, will formally exchange the documents today. (2) The Turkish Chargé d'Affaires has returned to his country on the order of his government. The Turkish embassy in China has temporarily suspended its offices because no one is in charge. Because no one is acting as an agent for the Sino-Turkish treaty, the future signing can only be executed in Europe, probably at an embassy in Paris or Geneva, where the Turkish representative stationed there will jointly sign. (3) The agreement on the recovery of the French Concession in Shanghai is expected to be signed next week. (4) Regarding the issue of the suspension of war debt payments in Europe, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs has telegraphed Rong Kui, the agent stationed in the United States, to investigate because it is not aware of its scope. (5) During his visit to Beijing, in addition to negotiating the Korean case, Chongguang raised the issue of legal rights between China and Japan. Our side submitted an answer to Chongguang to forward to the Japanese government.

Policy of Invading Manchuria and Mongolia

Russo-Japanese Transportation Conference

Will Be Held in Harbin at the End of August

Russia and Japan Join Forces to Counteract Huludao

Osaka Correspondence: In order to resolve the railway disputes between Russia and Japan over the past 27 years, Japan has decided to hold a Russo-Japanese transportation conference in Harbin at the end of August. The participating organizations will be the Japanese Ministry of Railways, Mantetsu, Korean Railways, Kita Nippon Steamship, Osaka Shosen, the Chinese Eastern Railway, and the Siberian Railway Authority. The aim of the discussion is the competition for the export of goods through the ports of Dalian, Vladivostok, and Korea. For the sake of the prosperity of Vladivostok, the Soviet Union advocated that all goods from northern Manchuria exported to Japan via the Chinese Eastern Railway should pass through Suifenhe to Vladivostok for export, without passing through Korean Railways or Dalian, because the freight is 15% to 45% lower than that of the Japanese railway. However, Mantetsu believes that it has suffered great losses as a result. Therefore, Mantetsu convened a Eurasian Joint Transport Conference in Tokyo in early July. As a result of the meeting, the Japanese strongly opposed the freight rate between Manzhouli, Suifenhe, and Vladivostok proposed by Russia, but the Russians also vehemently rejected the freight rate between Manzhouli, Andong, and Dalian proposed by the Japanese. Both sides have reserved the two cases. The Japanese are now vigorously promoting to the Russian side that the state-owned railway laid by China between Huludao and Qiqihar will soon be completed. In the future, the export goods from northern Manchuria will be taken away by the Chinese railway and exported through Huludao, and the Chinese Eastern Railway and the South Manchurian Railway will suffer the same pain. Therefore, Russia and Japan need to unite to counteract Huludao and open up this difficult situation and resolve the previous splits between Russia and Japan. Based on this propaganda, the meeting will be held again.

中華民國二十年七月十八日 星期六（十一）<第三張H]

Republic of China, Year 20, July 18th, Saturday (11) [Third Sheet H]

News in Brief

Mantetsu convened a Russo-Japanese transportation conference in an effort to unify the freight rates of the railways of Russia and Japan, jointly counteracting the Chinese railways and carrying out the invasion of Manchuria and Mongolia. Thus, the collusion between Russia and Japan to plot against us is becoming increasingly urgent. (July 14th)

Troops from Jin and Li

Pursue Mutinous Troops of Gao Guizi's Command

Two Companies from Feng's Division Also Cooperating in the Attack

Taiyuan Correspondence: After the mutiny in Pingding, Gao Guizi's troops were immediately pursued by other units and fled to Yu County. Recently, a small unit fled to Wutai, looting along the way. Li Fuying, Division Commander of the Fifth Division, considering Wutai to be his division's defense area, feared that the bandit soldiers would wander and harass Dingxiang, Yan County, and Xin County. In addition to telegraphing Li Zaixi's regiment to rush to Taihua Town, Wutai City, and Ekou, which belongs to Dai County, to block the bandit soldiers, he specially took a special car with several adjutants to Yuanping and went to the front line for inspection yesterday. According to Li's report when he left Jing yesterday morning, Tan Benren's trip to the front line was entirely for the sake of public security. In addition to taking his adjutants Xing Shuqian and Chang Wenxiang, he also had several detectives and ten grooms. After arriving in Yuanping, he planned to send several officers to the Wutai area to urge the various units to find ways to block and suppress the bandit soldiers, and send detectives to secretly search for them in the area where the defeated soldiers passed, determined not to allow anyone to hide. It is reported that two companies of Feng Pengzhu's troops have now rushed to Bolin Town to assist in the encirclement and suppression. It is thought that these few defeated soldiers will be easily resolved soon. As for the details of the rebellion in Pingding by the troops, the report from that side is as follows: It is reported that most of the officers and soldiers of Gao's division's Han unit are students, and some of them have been instigated by the communists. This time, the mutiny of the second battalion of the first regiment was initiated by the company commander Liu. As for the soldiers, most of them blindly followed. This action was purely directed and controlled by junior officers. On the evening of the 4th, before the soldiers' mutiny, the师特务连某头目 (chief of the division's special service company, sergeant or lower) reported to the division headquarters. Jin, the staff officer, then deployed defenses. Fortunately, the situation did not spread. It is learned that the mutinous soldiers had made a plan to rebel the previous month and then decided to riot at 12:00 p.m. on the 4th of this month. That morning, they used small leaflets to notify a certain chief of the special service company to take a bath in the bathhouse, so as to reach the time of the riot (12:00 p.m. on the 4th). Then, a certain chief immediately reported to the division headquarters. The division headquarters made timely preparations for defense. The mutinous soldiers learned that the matter had been leaked and changed the scheduled time to two points earlier (10:00 p.m.) to take action. At that time, the mutinous soldiers formed a team to attack the upper city (the headquarters was stationed there). When they reached the city slope, it happened that the division headquarters had also moved the special service company and the military police company to protect the headquarters and sent another elite force to defend the point commission residence (the point commission was stationed in Pingding Middle School in the upper city). Two machine guns were also placed in front of the city building in the upper city. When the mutinous soldiers arrived, they immediately opened fire and pounced. They were immediately swept by machine guns on the city. The mutinous soldiers suffered more than ten casualties. Knowing that it was difficult to succeed, they retreated and gathered in Dongguan, fleeing in panic and unable to rob the citizens. This was a great fortune. The mutinous soldiers fled through Baiyangshu Station at 1:00 a.m. on the 4th and fled to Yu County early in the morning on the 5th. On the 7th, it was heard that the pursuit team sent by the division and the artillery unit stationed in Yu County had jointly surrounded and defeated them. The troops of Feng Pengzhu stationed in Jingxing were also notified to find ways to cooperate in the attack. They are now trailing. It is said that the mutinous soldiers are still entrenched in Shipan Mountain (between Jingxing and Yu County). The division has telegraphed the troops stationed in Shijiazhuang and other places to find ways to block the pursuit. (13th)

Cultural Exhibition by Daming Lake

Brick and Tile, and Book Exhibition

Jinan Correspondence: The Shandong Provincial Library, in order to awaken the public's attention to and interest in preserving antiquities and culture, is preparing to hold an antiquities exhibition. It has now been decided to hold two exhibitions simultaneously from the 21st of this month: one is the Qin and Han Brick and Tile Exhibition, and the other is the Rare Book Exhibition. The exhibition period is three days and is open to the public, but in reality, what is exhibited is not only bricks, tiles, and books. The content of the exhibition includes: (1) Qin and Han bricks and tiles collected by the Gao family in Weixian, that is, those confiscated by the Department of Education in Qingdao, with the addition of Pan Gu Xiaolu tile end texts compiled by Xu Yinlin and the same brick texts; (2) Pottery pieces from Chengziya, that is, the antiquities obtained from the ancient Tanzi country in Longshan Town, which was excavated last winter; (3) Ancient coins from Luo Gu Lou, that is, those collected by Ma Guohan of Jinan Yuhan Shufang and now preserved in the library; (4) Han paintings, that is, those discovered in Teng County before the military incident last year, and those collected by the library over the years; (5) Books: (1) Old collections of the Haiyuan Pavilion of the Yang family in Liaocheng, which were scattered after the bandit riots and purchased by the library; (2) Antiquities of the Ming Dynasty Wenyuange, that is, butterfly-bound books stored in the old Qing Cabinet Treasury, which were purchased by the library this year; (3) Other rare books collected by Ma Huijie over the years, which were purchased by the library for 120,000 yuan, as well as rare books purchased sporadically one after another. Qilu is a cultural region with many antiquities. Since Luo Zhengjun founded the Shandong Library in Shandong during the former Qing Dynasty, the library has collected considerable amounts of bronze inscriptions, calligraphy, and paintings over the years. Since the current curator, Wang Xiantang, took office, Wang, who is proficient in bronze inscriptions, calligraphy, and paintings, has painstakingly collected and managed them, and the provincial government has been able to allocate large sums of money to enable the library to purchase them at any time. Thus, the ancient fragrance by Daming Lake competes with the scenery of mountains and rivers. This exhibition will be able to give the society immeasurable pleasure and give the public a good opportunity to speculate and test their cultural imagination. In order to expand publicity, the library specially wrote an article of more than 10,000 words on why bricks, tiles, and books should be exhibited, explaining the meaning of the exhibition and hoping to arouse the public's desire for knowledge of culture.

Bengbu Has Become a Waterland

The Disaster in Zhengyangguan Is Also Extremely Serious

Bengbu Correspondence: Continuous heavy rains and mountain floods in northern Anhui caused the Jiaojiang River to rise upstream of the Changhuai River, in the area of Fuyang, Zhengyang, and Sanhejian. Several places rose and the water surged downwards, flowing very turbulently. Although the weather here has been clear since the 13th, the water level of the Huai River has continued to rise. Today it increased by two feet, and it is already level with the bank. The water situation on the north and south banks east of the Iron Bridge is also tense. Several places have breached and overflowed, and the water flows horizontally, making it impossible to stop it. All the dikes have been submerged by the water. The water and the sky are the same color, and the wilderness is indistinguishable. The water north of Xiaobengbu is a vast expanse of water, and the autumn crops in the fields are all submerged. The sorghum in the water is already four or five feet high and only the tops are visible. The water on the south bank of Henan has poured into the city. The area around the east amusement park is like being in a water country. The thatched huts of the poor are like floating on the water. Large ships on the Huai River sailed into it and moored under the high embankment of the railway. The sails are like a forest. The Yaohua Electric Light Company is completely surrounded by water. The residents nearby rely entirely on sampans for transportation. Tangyuan has become a pool. Small boats sailed to the north end of Guofu Street and stopped at the entrance of Tangyuan. All the shops on Huachang Street, Deheli, Damalu, Zhengzhong Street, Ermalu, and Laodajie were flooded, and the drivers waded through the water, which was knee-deep. The scale of the flood can be imagined. The new straw sheds built by the victims on the vacant land north of Shunhe Street and the horizontal railway are countless, sheltering themselves from the wind and dew with wooden racks and mats. The Bengbu Flood Relief Committee has been very busy in recent days providing relief to the victims. Yesterday and today, it distributed relief funds at the General Chamber of Commerce, disbursing more than 4,000 yuan. The remaining victims who have not received the relief are still being investigated. Zhengyangguan, upstream, is an area where the waters of the Huai, Ying, and Fei Rivers converge. The land is low-lying. It is reported that due to continuous heavy rains and the Jiaojiang River rising in Sanhejian, the torrents poured down, causing the entire town to become a waterland. Four-tenths of the city walls collapsed, and five-tenths of the houses collapsed. The streets and markets are as if sailing in a river. The severity of the disaster is unprecedented in sixty years. At present, the water level is still rising without receding. I do not know when it will end. (July 15th)

Local Correspondence

Songjiang

Mining of Stones in Jiufeng Forbidden: The Jiufeng Mountains are located between Songjiang and Qingpu counties. There are many historical sites and they have long been known as scenic spots. The local residents near the area eyed the mountain stones and went to the official property bureau to apply for land to mine. Citizens of Qingpu, such as Ni Zhuhua, He Pancang, Zhao Pingao, and Sheng Langxi, petitioned the Ministry of Internal Affairs and the Ministry of Finance to prohibit stone mining in order to protect the historical sites and maintain public safety. This newspaper has learned that the Ministry of Finance has instructed the Jiangsu Department of Finance to instruct the Songjinqing Official Property Branch Bureau and the Songjiang and Qingpu County Governments to prohibit it. The instruction is as follows: "In order to comply with the order, Ni Zhuhua et al. submitted a petition requesting a strict order to prohibit stone mining in Jiufeng's scenic spots to protect historical sites and maintain public safety." In addition to approving the petition and learning about the preservation of scenic spots and historical sites, which is within the scope of internal affairs, it should be directly submitted to the Ministry of Internal Affairs for investigation and verification. If there is any stone mining on the Jiufeng Mountain land released by the former Official Property Office, it should be prohibited at any time. It should be ordered that the Jiangsu Department of Finance follow the instructions and instruct the Songjinqing Official Property Branch Bureau and the Songjiang and Qingpu County Governments to follow this order."

Record of the Party and Government Discussion Meeting: The County Executive Committee and the County Government and various bureaus held the 25th Party and Government Discussion Meeting in the County Government on the 16th. Sun Shiheng, Lu Zhichang, and Lu Changlin of the Party Committee, County Magistrate Shen Yong, and the heads of the various bureaus all attended. County Magistrate Shen chaired the meeting. Matters discussed: (1) The County Executive Committee's proposal to build the Sun Yat-sen Memorial Hall has been proposed for a long time but has not been implemented. How should it be quickly prepared? As a result, the county government will investigate the case and submit it to the provincial government to order the dispatch of personnel to come to Song to investigate and determine the case in order to build it. (2) The County Executive Committee proposed that the building of the big guard post in front of the County Government is not suitable and obstructs traffic. Please demolish it as soon as possible. As a result, the county magistrate should order the Construction Bureau to demolish it immediately and submit a report to the hall for record. (3) The County Executive Committee proposed that the crude paper merchants Tu Shunchou et al. submitted a petition stating that the tax collection was unsuccessful and that they were deliberately oppressing the people. Please maintain it and send a letter to the Public Security Bureau and the District Office to revoke the deadline for eviction, etc. The committee decided to submit it to the Party and Government Discussion Meeting. How should it be handled? As a result, the original method proposed by the Health Committee will still be followed, and the discussion and ban methods of each point in the original petition will be submitted to the county for review.

Punishment for Singing Tanhuang: Han Xiaozhou, a staff member of the Third District Office of the county, used the name of raising funds in Xinqiao Town to sing Tanhuang, which was about to cause trouble. The county government inquired about it and sent police captain Chen Rongchu to investigate secretly. It was true, but it had already been stopped. County Magistrate Shen believed that Han, as a staff member of the District Office, was absurd in such behavior, so he recorded a major demerit. The district chief should be reprimanded for failing to detect it in advance and failing to stop it afterwards.

Suzhou

Li Mingyang Comes to Suzhou to Investigate Mutinous Soldiers: Li Mingyang, the Director of the Jiangsu Provincial Security Office, arrived in Suzhou after Zhu Mian, the Commander of the Taihu Bandit Suppression and concurrently Head of the Provincial Security First Regiment, telegraphed that the Second Company of the First Battalion of the Fourth Security Regiment, stationed in Pingwang for bandit suppression, had conspired with Henan gang bandits to stage a mutiny on the fourteenth night. Fortunately, Battalion Commander Shao Rencheng detected it early and disarmed the mutinous soldiers. They were escorted to Suzhou on the sixteenth, and the ringleaders were captured and are undergoing strict interrogation. Battalion Commander Shao has also been temporarily placed under surveillance pending investigation to ensure local peace and stability. Li arrived in Suzhou from Zhenjiang at 2 PM yesterday (the seventeenth) to investigate and it is said that Li also brought a company of soldiers from the Seventh Company of the Third Battalion of the First Regiment, expected to arrive in Suzhou at 6 PM that night.

Robbery Occurs Outside Changmen: At approximately 1 AM on the seventeenth, four or five individuals dressed in tattered military uniforms suddenly appeared at the home of Du Runsheng, a chopstick maker in Bailianqiao Alley outside Changmen. They silenced the family members and arbitrarily searched the premises, injuring Du Runsheng. Before leaving, they also snatched a gold bracelet from Du's daughter-in-law, Ms. Shen. Afterwards, the victim reported the incident to the Public Security Bureau for investigation.

Wuxi

Plainclothes Police Arrest Gamblers, Sparking a Riot: Recently, gambling and skimming have been rampant in the Erfang Langxia teahouse near Yanjiaqiao in the eighth district of the county. The sixteenth branch of the district's Public Security Bureau became aware of this, and Bureau Chief Xia Chungang dispatched employee Liang Cuiting and patrol officer Peng Xialing with police to investigate. They apprehended four gamblers and gambling paraphernalia on the spot. As they were about to escort them back to the bureau, over a hundred villagers bravely rushed forward, surrounded them, and snatched the four captured gamblers. Then, Tu Zheng (local head) Yu Yulin, fearing that the police were imposters due to their lack of uniforms, urgently rushed to Patrol Officer Liu Ziyan of the third sub-division of the second squadron of the police brigade stationed in the town, reporting that communists were rioting and requesting assistance. Patrol Officer Liu, upon receiving the report, quickly led police to the teahouse. There, they found seven people surrounded by villagers. Liu immediately inquired and learned they were officers arresting gamblers under orders, and that they were trapped. Tu Zheng Yu Yulin testified that the town was robbed by communists in April of the previous year and that four men and women were kidnapped and only released after several months. He claimed that the police were not wearing uniforms, had no official business, and might be up to no good, hence the request for their arrest. Patrol Officer Liu, based on the testimony, escorted the seven officers, including Liang Cuiting, along with Tu Zheng Yu Yulin, to the brigade headquarters. Public Security Bureau Chief Xia Chungang also prepared a written report and submitted it to the Public Security Bureau, requesting an investigation.

County Magistrate's Daughter-in-Law Requests Divorce: Yang Zhonghan, a native of this county, served as the Magistrate of Wujiang County when Sun Chuanfang governed Suzhou. His son, Baochun, fell in love with Ms. Yu Ranxian and lived with her. They formally married in the winter of the 17th year [of the Republic, i.e. 1928]. They were very happy together, but both suffered from syphilis and often went to Shanghai for treatment. Recently, Ms. Yu suddenly claimed that Yang Baochun smoked red pills (heroin) and that his lower body was infected with syphilis. She hired a lawyer and sued the county court for divorce, requesting alimony of 30,000 yuan and the return of her dowry worth 4,000 yuan. Yesterday was the date for the court hearing, and the people of the county, impressed by Ms. Yu's reputation, crowded to listen. During the hearing, Judge Liang first heard Ms. Yu Ranxian recount the history of their love and state her purpose, while Yang Baochun claimed that he did not have venereal disease initially and only contracted it after engaging in carnal relations with the plaintiff. Lawyers from both sides debated the results. Judge Liang ordered the plaintiff to instruct the defendant to go to the hospital for verification.

Changzhou

Police Team Opens Fire on Bandits: On the evening of the fourteenth, the home of Chen Zhaosheng in Chenjia Lane, fourth district of Wujin County, was robbed by bandits who kidnapped Chen Zhaosheng to Chenshu Village and released him. Zhaosheng's elderly mother died of fright. Upon receiving this report, Captain Yu of the First Squadron of the police team stationed in Panshu Town learned that a ransom of 1,000 yuan was to be paid at Shuang Gou Dam in front of Chenshu on the evening of the sixteenth, with a red lantern as the signal. That evening, at around 8 PM, Captain Yu led fifty to sixty officers from the second and third squadrons, dividing their forces and heading out. They arrived near Shuang Gou Dam around 11 PM and saw over thirty people gathered in the field. When the police team approached and asked for the password, the bandits did not answer. The police immediately fired warning shots, and the bandits returned fire. The two sides exchanged fire for about an hour before the bandits retreated. As a result, the bandit Pang Quansheng was shot and killed in the river. A Mauser pistol was found next to Pang. On the police side, officers Lin Qiuqi and Xu Shubiao were wounded by bullets passing through their feet. Some of the bandits were also injured and carried away by their comrades. Pang Quansheng was a notorious bandit from Baitutang, Jiangyin County, and the county government had offered a 500 yuan reward for his arrest. Pang's body was recovered and transported to the city by boat on the seventeenth for identification. The wounded officers were also sent to the hospital for treatment.

Zhenjiang

Tobacco and Alcohol Merchants Oppose Excessive Taxes: Zhenjiang tobacco and alcohol merchants and citizens, angered by the excessive and disruptive taxes levied by the Tobacco and Alcohol License Tax Collection Office, held a general meeting in the county party headquarters auditorium yesterday at 3 PM. Over 400 people attended, chaired by Wang Zhaoru. The meeting resolved the following four points: (1) Representatives from large and small tobacco and alcohol merchants will be appointed to negotiate directly with the Tobacco and Alcohol Tax Office. (2) They will only reluctantly agree to pay taxes at the previous rates. (3) If negotiations are unsuccessful, a second general meeting will be convened. (4) Each tobacco and alcohol merchant will post a notice at their door stating "Awaiting Resolution by the Association" to show solidarity.

Re-examination of Wang Yuanchen's Case: Wang Yuanchen, the Director of the Provincial Hospital, was previously sued by Yi Ruichang in the Zhenjiang District Court for neglect of duty. It is reported that the court issued a large number of summonses yesterday, summoning all relevant parties to a retrial scheduled for the seventeenth.

Melon Farmers Request Urgent Allocation of Funds to Build Embankments: Due to continuous rain in the past half-month, the riverbanks of Guazhou and Hedong in Zhenjiang have repeatedly collapsed, inundating hundreds of acres of farmland. Residents in the weirs have been forced to relocate. With the water level rising daily, Liu Changchun and Zhang Zhao, citizens residing in the province, have petitioned the provincial government to quickly allocate 5,000 yuan to urgently build new embankments to protect the people's lives.

Yangzhou

Telegram Reporting Bandit Suppression Victory in Suining: Zhang Zhijiang, the Pacification Commissioner, received a telegram from Ma Renxing, the Chief of Staff of the Third Cavalry Division in Suining, reporting that over a hundred bandits attacked and captured Houwang Village on the night of [the reported date] and occupied the blockhouse. The division commander led troops to suppress them, reaching the vicinity of Zhangjia Temple around noon. The attack continued until 9 PM, when artillery fire was used. The bandits, taking advantage of the night, attempted to flee through the inner and outer moats. Our forces intercepted them, causing the bandits to scatter. It is estimated that dozens of bandits were killed and over ten, including the fake company commander Xu Buqing, were captured alive. Many spoils of war were seized. It is reported that the bandits have fled to the area south of the Long River. Troops have been dispatched to Xiaxu, Qianwang Village, and other places to investigate the bandits' whereabouts.

Tong Qinghe Rice Shop Robbed: At approximately 9 PM the night before last, five or six bandits suddenly appeared at the Tong Qinghe Rice Shop in Hebei, Xiannvmiao Town, brandishing pistols and making loud noises. They rushed into the shop, silencing everyone, and arbitrarily searched the counter, robbing a total of ninety-eight yuan in silver dollars, one yuan and three dimes in paper money, and nineteen dimes in small silver coins. The fourth branch of the Public Security Bureau dispatched police to pursue the bandits upon hearing the alarm, but they had already fled without a trace.

Nantong

County Government Escorts Prisoners, Causing Uproar in Jail: The Nantong County Government received over seventy prisoners involved in the local purge case and counter-revolutionaries escorted back from Suzhou, all detained in the temporary prison at the Clock Tower. At 2 AM on the morning of the sixteenth, the prisoners in the prison rioted, breaking many of the iron bars of their cells. Warden Zhou Liancheng immediately reported to the county government, which dispatched police to suppress the riot, preventing any incidents. After daybreak, Li Qi, Tang Yugao, and others were interrogated by the county authorities, all claiming the uproar was due to prisoners' delirium and misunderstandings. County Magistrate Zhang has ordered shackles to be placed on the ringleaders and is transferring the key prisoners in the banditry case to Zhenjiang today for trial by military law.

Local Guard Tightens Budget: Nantong's local finances are short by 60,000 yuan. Despite temporarily increasing business donations, there is still a deficit. The county government has approved the resolution of various agencies, ordering the Public Security Bureau and the county police force on the sixteenth to each reduce their annual budgets by 12,000 yuan. All district defense forces will be immediately reorganized, using mandatory conscription.

Taicang

Dispute in Taicang Shipping Industry: Mr. Huang and others from this county believed that there was still a need for a steamship route from Shatou to Kunshan via Zhoushi. To facilitate transportation, they founded the Kunxing Steamship Company, obtained a license from the Ministry of Transportation, a permit for inland waters from the Jianghai Customs, and filed with the Kunshan and Taicang county governments and the Construction Bureau, requesting an operating permit. However, a Mr. Li, who claims to be from the shipping industry association, filed a petition with the Taicang county government, claiming that the ship's hull was narrow and its materials were substandard, attacking its safety. It is said that the manager of the Kunxing Steamship refuted this claim, stating that the Kunxing Steamship had been inspected by customs and found to be safe. The Jianghai Customs issued a permit allowing it to operate, and only the Jianghai Customs ship inspection office has the authority to determine the safety of a vessel. Mr. Li and others from the shipping industry association were acting unreasonably and creating trouble without understanding the situation. It is also said that the Qin Yu and Da Liang steamships also lack operating permits.

Jiangyin

County Government Meeting Discusses Flood Relief: Since the continuous heavy rains, most of the low-lying weir fields in the four townships have been flooded, and reports of disasters have been sent to the county government. The most severely affected areas include: the banks of the Sihe River in three sections, the Jiuqing Weir which is damaged, over 70 zhang of the dike, over 20 zhang of the Majiaba dike, over 10 zhang of the Wangjiaba dike, and over 50 zhang of the Xiaoqingci dike. The northern and southern weirs in Zhouzhuang Township are a vast expanse of water. Along the canal, from Nanzha Gate to Sihe Gate, the banks have collapsed in low-lying areas, making passage impossible, and in high-lying areas, they have collapsed like cliffs, making the route as dangerous as the roads of Shu. On the fourteenth, the county government meeting discussed the issue. County Magistrate Peng proposed that in addition to sending telegrams to the district chiefs to investigate and report on the damage and rescue efforts, the chief of the Second Section, Jiang Wuyi, along with the directors of the Construction Bureau and the Finance Bureau, should go to the countryside to survey the flood damage. The contractors of Licheng and Yandong Three Small Steamboat Companies were ordered to quickly allocate the funds agreed upon in the past to provide relief and rebuild.

Charitable Property Dispute Resolved After Several Years: The dispute over the charitable property under the name of the first district office's Public Charity Hall, which the Relief Institute was to receive, has been unresolved for several years. After Zhu Tianying became the district chief, the transfer issue centered on the establishment of a management committee to implement independent management of the city property. Before the previous day, County Magistrate Peng convened Relief Institute Director Cao Yuanmo and District Chief Zhu Tianying, strongly urging both sides to refrain from further written attacks. Both parties drafted a simplified charter for the management committee. On the fourteenth, the county government sent Section Chief Jin and Clerk Xie to supervise District Chief Zhu in transferring the aid register, documents, and books under the name of the Public Charity Hall to the Relief Institute.

Gaoyou

Education Bureau Chief's Resignation Approved: Sun Weixian, the Education Bureau Chief of this county, has worked diligently since taking office. Recently, due to a certain incident, he resigned to the Education Department. His resignation has been approved. Director Sun returned to You yesterday evening and will hand over his duties as soon as a new appointment is made.

Bandits Rob and Injure Person in Lijiazhuang: At approximately 9 PM the night before last, six or seven bandits armed with guns suddenly appeared at the home of Lin Zihou, a farmer in Lijiazhuang, ninth district of the county. They kicked down the door and ransacked the house. The losses are said to be considerable. Lin's wife resisted the bandits and was seriously injured.

Hangzhou

Smuggling of Narcotics Ring Cracked: Zhejiang Provincial Government Chairman Zhang Nanxian received a tip that the Huachang Paint Factory at No. 22 Qingnian Road, New Market, was a major drug smuggling center. Yesterday (the seventeenth) at 9 AM, he dispatched Huang Bingxun, the chief of the Second Section of the Civil Affairs Department, along with He Yunshang, the director of the Provincial Capital Public Security Bureau, Zhu Huiqing, a representative of the Chamber of Commerce, and over a dozen patrol officers to search the factory. They successfully uncovered a massive quantity of opium and heroin, including over a dozen large wooden crates with National Government registration marks, seventy-six iron boxes, and over one hundred and twenty paper packages, all containing the drugs. They also found seals from the Jiangsu Construction Department. Patrol Team Leader Zhong Jixing and Second District Director Tong Dianmei also arrived upon hearing the news. They ordered the police to load the drugs into police vehicles and seal up the remaining non-contraband items in the factory, along with the building itself. The factory manager, Huang Liquan, and his partner, Li Shengqing, were arrested and taken to the Public Security Bureau for questioning, after which they will be transferred to the court for strict prosecution according to the law.

Bribery in Selling Tobacco Seedlings Announced: Zhang Zuhuai, the director of the Yongkang Xianyou Public Security Branch in Zhejiang Province, led police to Babao Mountain, accepted bribes, and privately sold tobacco seedlings. The county discovered this and arrested Zhang, sending him to the Civil Affairs Department to be punished by the Hangzhou District Court according to the law. After several investigations by the Criminal Court, Judge Liao Wen pronounced the sentence yesterday in court, sentencing Zhang Zuhuai to four years in prison for accepting bribes and ordering him to be returned to prison to await execution.

Major Theft Case in Hu Shu, Caoying Lane: The Zhang Yiyi silversmith workshop in Caoying Lane, Hu Shu, was burglarized yesterday at 3 AM. Thieves dug through the back door and stole over a hundred taels of broken silver, a gold-inlaid jade ring, and a set of ceremonial robes worth over 140 yuan, along with other clothing and items, for a total loss of 700 yuan. Muddy footprints were left on the door panel and table. Mr. Zhang has reported the loss and requested the detective team and the responsible police station to investigate.

Shangyu

Continuation of Banditry in Siming Mountain: The rampant banditry in Siming Mountain, at the intersection of three counties, continues. According to further reports, on the evening of the sixth of this month, in Dongjia'an Taoshu, near the bandits' den, a mother and son (the mother was eighty years old and the son twenty-three) were roasting tea leaves when over twenty bandits broke in. They first killed the son, then stripped the old woman naked and threw her into the tea-roasting stove, placing dry wood underneath and burning her alive. In addition, a Mr. Tong from Sheng County was kidnapped by bandits and taken to the mountains, where they forced him to write a letter to his family demanding a ransom of 60,000 yuan. When this was not paid, they abandoned his body in a mountain stream. Recently, villages such as Yujiakeng, Chengdakeng, Kaokeng, and Pingkeng have been alarmed several times a day. Villagers have either moved their families far away or hid in dense grass or slept in the open fields. The situation is extremely dire. It is reported that the bandits are equipped with sophisticated firearms, including many firearms for a small number of people. They wear wooden holsters around their waists and carry rifles on their shoulders, and they also have grenades and machine guns. This should not be ignored.

Huzhou

Petition to Provincial Government for Joint Efforts to Arrest Huzhou Bandits: Wang Zhiqi, commander of the Second Regiment of the Huzhou Security Team and deputy commander of the temporary command for joint bandit suppression in Taihu Lake, previously received reports from detectives and confessions from captured bandits that many notorious bandits who had not been apprehended were hiding in Shanghai and elsewhere. Wang Zhiqi immediately petitioned the provincial civil affairs department to request the Jiangsu provincial government to jointly assist in the arrest.

Pinghu

Sister-in-Law Conspires to Murder Disabled Brother-in-Law: The case of Shao Basanguan from Hanmiao, whose eyes were gouged out by thugs at the instigation of his sister-in-law, Shao Ni, has been pending in the county government for several weeks since Basanguan filed his complaint. Shao's elder brother, Shao Kejie, has been secretly using his influence to stall the case. Basanguan initially lived in the South Gate Hospital of the city, but unable to afford the expenses, he moved into the home of his elder brother, Shao Kejie. Unexpectedly, Shao Ni harbored sinister intentions and plotted to assassinate Basanguan and silence him. On the night before the previous day, she took advantage of him sleeping soundly and summoned a thug named Shi Azhao, who stealthily entered Basanguan's room with a pig-slaughtering knife, intending to kill him. Fortunately, Basanguan woke up, cried out for help, and neighbors gathered, capturing Shi and finding the sharp weapon. The thug was handed over to the village committee for punishment by the county.

Ningbo

Jiangdong Xiamao Pond Robbery: Chen Xiaocai, a resident of Jiangdong Xiamao Pond in this port city, runs the Hexing Leather Shop on Baojia Daotou. He and Xu Song are neighbors and have similar economic circumstances. At 1 AM yesterday morning, while they were sound asleep, five or six bandits armed with handguns broke through the back door and ransacked the houses for two hours. The total losses for both families are estimated to be around 3,000 yuan.

Port Organizes Anti-Japanese Support Association: Since the Wanbaoshan Incident, various circles in the port have been extremely indignant. In addition to the county party headquarters and the [service] unit issuing a circular announcing the various crimes of the Japanese in instigating Koreans to massacre overseas Chinese, the [service] unit and others initiated a call for various circles to organize an Anti-Japanese Support Association to sever economic ties with Japan and serve as a backing for diplomacy.

Educational News

Important News

Ministry Order

Selecting and Dispatching Supervisors to Inspect Social Education

The Ministry of Education issued a notice to the education departments and bureaus of various provinces and cities, selecting and dispatching supervisors to specifically inspect the implementation of social education in their jurisdictions, or to pay special attention to verifying the actual situation during regional inspections and reporting the details. They should also report on the implementation situation at the end of each semester for assessment. The notice stated, "Now is the period of political tutelage, and social education is extremely important. All relevant facilities have been planned and promulgated, and local education administrative agencies have earnestly complied with the orders, while others have ignored them. In order to conduct detailed assessments and promote implementation, the Ministry hereby orders your department to select and dispatch supervisors to conduct detailed inspections of the implementation of social education in your jurisdiction, or to pay special attention to verifying the actual situation during regional inspections and reporting the details. The inspection items should comply with the items stipulated in the social education investigation and statistics form previously issued by the Ministry, and refer to the needs of local examinations to prepare a form to be issued to each supervisor for verification, filling in, and submission for review. After receiving the aforementioned reports, each department should use them to assess the performance of its jurisdiction and determine rewards and punishments, and use them as a basis for future improvements. All implementation conditions should be reported for assessment at the end of each semester, no later than one month for cities directly under the Executive Yuan and no later than two months for other departments. Please comply with this order."

Local News

Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau Notice

Students Should Not Enter Unregistered Private Schools

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau issued a notice stating, "Now is the summer vacation, and many young students are preparing to apply to schools for further studies or transfers. When applying, it is important to investigate whether the schools are well-managed. If they are private schools, it is even more important to first inquire whether they are registered. Students from unregistered private schools are not accepted for transfer or further studies in public and registered private schools. Graduates from unregistered private schools cannot apply for overseas study examinations, civil service examinations, general examinations, or various civil servant technical personnel examinations. They are also unqualified to serve as staff in various agencies or teachers in various schools. Therefore, entering an unregistered private school now will cause many difficulties in future education and employment. Rather than facing difficulties later, it is better to be cautious and prudent when applying now. The Bureau will follow the Ministry of Education's instructions to ban private schools that refuse to register. We hope that parents of students will pay attention to the schools that their children apply to and not enter unregistered private schools again. This is of great importance to your children's future, so please do not ignore it."

Shanghai Municipal Council

Appoints Yang Nielingyu as Principal of Girls' Middle School

The Shanghai Municipal Council's newly established Girls' Middle School initially appointed Yu Qingtang as principal. The Shanghai Vocational Guidance Center's recent work in vocational counseling, educational guidance, talent registration, employee testing, legal guidance, and health guidance has been extremely busy. Van Hang's Skills Weakened

Commercial University Fortunate to Win

Result: 34 to 31, Defeating Van Hang

Tonight at 8 PM at the Original Field, War Eagles Team

The Commercial University basketball team played Van Hang last night at 8 PM at the China Basketball Hall. Over 400 spectators, half Japanese and half Chinese, watched the game. The strength of the two teams was far superior to Van Hang, but the circumstances of each team were different. One team had been out of competition for a long time, while the other was in training. Commercial University's victory was entirely due to luck. If played another day, Van Hang would win easily. The result was 34 to 31, Commercial University won. Referee: Jiang Xiangqing.

Van Hang Sweats to Fight Stubborn Enemy

Diao Youdao Shows His Ability, Qian Jingyong Plays as a Guest

The Van Hang generals had not been on the battlefield for a long time, and their weapons had already rusted. At that time, it was inevitable that they would be unfamiliar with the game. Diao Youdao showed his ability and repeatedly broke through the enemy camp. Qian Jingyong's guest appearance greatly increased the team's strength. He was trapped at the start but quickly moved up. Diao and Chen, old partners, repeatedly collaborated. The whole team used high passing to defeat the enemy. In the first half, they repeatedly gained the upper hand, leading 4 to 3, 8 to 6, and 13 to 8. The final score was 14 to 16, losing momentum due to a lack of energy. In the second half, Diao Youdao became excited and fiercely attacked the enemy's fortress, scoring five goals in a row, a total of seven goals, making him the highest scorer in the two teams. At that time, the two sides were only one point apart. Before the last six minutes, Van Hang was still leading 30 to 27, but due to a lack of strength and fatigue, they watched the enemy become active and win. However, skill is one thing, and victory or defeat is another. One cannot simply judge heroes by victory or defeat.
