Promulgation of the Shanghai Municipality's Academic Calendar for the 20th Year

Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau Instruction Letter No. 741 to all municipal public and private schools at all levels: Regarding the city's academic calendar for the 20th year, this bureau previously, in accordance with the Ministry's promulgated revised regulations on the school year, semesters, and holiday dates, compiled and submitted it to the Ministry of Education and the Municipal Government for review. Now, we have received instructions approving it for record. Therefore, we are copying and issuing this order to all levels of schools in this city for unified compliance. Attached is a copy of the Shanghai Municipal Academic Calendar for the 20th year.

Shanghai Municipal Academic Calendar for the 20th Year

August 1st, Year 20 (Saturday) - First semester begins. 15th (Saturday) - Primary and secondary schools begin processing entrance examinations. 20th (Thursday) - Martyr Liao Zhongkai's Martyrdom Memorial Day (no holiday). Send representatives to participate in the Municipal Party Headquarters' memorial service. 22nd (Saturday) - Primary schools' first semester begins. 25th (Tuesday) - Secondary schools' first semester begins. 27th (Thursday) - Confucius' Birthday Memorial Day (holiday). Hold commemorative ceremonies and lectures on Confucius' life. September 9th (Wednesday) - Premier's First Uprising Memorial (no holiday). Send representatives to participate in the Municipal Party Headquarters' memorial service. 21st (Monday) - Martyr Zhu Zhixin's Martyrdom Memorial Day (no holiday). Send representatives to participate in the Municipal Party Headquarters' memorial service. October 10th (Saturday) - National Day Commemoration (holiday). Hang flags, display decorations, gather for celebrations, and give lectures on the history of the founding of the Republic of China. 11th (Sunday) - Premier's London Peril Memorial Day (no holiday). Send representatives to participate in the Municipal Party Headquarters' memorial service. November 12th (Thursday) - Premier's Birthday Commemoration (holiday). Hang flags, celebrate, gather for commemoration, and give lectures on the Premier's revolutionary history. December 5th (Saturday) - Zhaohe Warship Uprising Memorial Day (no holiday). Send representatives to participate in the Municipal Party Headquarters' memorial service. January 1st, Year 21 (Friday) - Anniversary of the Founding of the Republic of China. Hang flags, display decorations, gather for celebrations, and give lectures on the Premier's nation-building history. Same day (Friday) - Year-end holiday begins for all levels of schools. 3rd (Sunday) - Year-end holiday ends for all levels of schools. 8th (Friday) - Secondary schools begin semester examinations. 9th (Saturday) - Primary schools begin semester examinations. 18th (Monday) - Winter vacation begins for all levels of schools. 31st (Sunday) - Winter vacation ends for all levels of schools. Same day (Sunday) - First semester ends. February 1st (Monday) - Second semester begins. Same day (Monday) - Primary and secondary schools begin processing entrance examinations. 3rd (Wednesday) - Primary schools' second semester begins. 4th (Thursday) - Secondary schools' second semester begins. March 12th (Saturday) - Premier's Death Anniversary (Arbor Day) (holiday). Gather to mourn, give lectures on the history of the Chinese Nationalist Party, and conduct afforestation publicity. 18th (Friday) - Beijing People's Memorial Day (no holiday). Send representatives to participate in the Municipal Party Headquarters' memorial service. 21st (Monday) - Local Memorial Day (holiday). Send representatives to participate in the Municipal Party Headquarters' memorial service. 29th (Tuesday) - Revolutionary Martyrs Memorial Day (holiday). Send representatives to participate in the Municipal Party Headquarters' memorial and commemorative services. April 1st (Friday) - Spring break begins for all levels of schools. 7th (Thursday) - Spring break ends for all levels of schools. 12th (Tuesday) - Party Purification Memorial Day (no holiday). Send representatives to participate in the Municipal Party Headquarters' memorial service. May 5th (Thursday) - Revolutionary Government Memorial Day (holiday). Hang flags, celebrate, gather for commemoration, and give lectures on the significance of the Premier's assumption of the Extraordinary Grand Presidency. 9th (Monday) - National Humiliation Memorial Day (no holiday). Gather to commemorate and give speeches on the origins of the [May Ninth], [August 29th], [September Seventh] National Humiliations and the [May Thirtieth], [June Second Third] Massacres, and the significance of abolishing unequal treaties. 18th (Wednesday) - Martyr Chen Yingshi's Memorial Day (no holiday). Send representatives to participate in the Municipal Party Headquarters' memorial service. June 3rd (Friday) - Anti-Drug Memorial Day (no holiday). Hang flags for commemoration, hold lectures on the efforts that citizens should make regarding drug resistance. 16th (Thursday) - Premier's Guangzhou Peril Memorial Day (no holiday). Send representatives to participate in the Municipal Party Headquarters' memorial service. Same day (Thursday) - Secondary schools begin processing matters for the end of the second semester. 18th (Saturday) - Primary schools begin processing matters for the end of the second semester. 30th (Thursday) - Summer vacation begins for secondary schools. July 3rd (Sunday) - Summer vacation begins for primary schools. 7th (Thursday) - Shanghai Municipal Government Establishment Anniversary (holiday). 9th (Saturday) - National Revolutionary Army Swearing-in Memorial Day (holiday). Hang flags, gather to celebrate, and give lectures on the historical mission of the National Revolutionary Army and the Northern Expedition. 31st (Sunday) - Second semester ends.

Explanations

(1) This calendar stipulates that summer vacation for middle schools is limited to 56 days, and for elementary schools to 50 days. Winter vacation for all levels of schools is set at 14 days, year-end vacation at 3 days, and spring vacation at 7 days. The total of 9 memorial holidays is in accordance with the Ministry of Education's promulgated revised regulations on school year, semesters, and holiday dates. (2) Each school's founding anniversary may be a holiday for one day. The 5th or 10th anniversary celebration may be a holiday for two days. (3) In addition to Sundays and stipulated holiday dates, arbitrary holidays or changes to holiday dates are not permitted. (4) Each school should fill in details of all kinds of memorial weeks and other gatherings, as well as all administrative matters related to the school, and compile them into the school calendar, reporting to this bureau for record.

South China Football Team's Southern Expedition to Java, Second Match (1)

Wins 3-2 Against Bandung Luno Team

(Xuelou from Bandung) The South China Football Team, renowned in Java, immediately embarked on an eastward expedition to Bandung the day after their draw in Batavia on June 7th. Their opponent was the Luno team, champions of Bandung. As a result, football fans from all over Java flocked to Bandung.

Much Discussion and Speculation About the Outcome

Before the battle commenced, there was much discussion on all sides regarding the outcome. One view was that South China's forwards were incredibly sharp and their defense was like an impregnable wall, so victory was assured. Another view was that Bandung teams have always had the reputation of being "fierce at home," and it is not easy for visiting teams, no matter how strong, to win. For example, the Lok Wah team did not achieve good results in either of their two visits. Even teams from other cities on the island, as strong as Surabaya, have often suffered defeats here. Even when the national team sends its elite to compete against individual teams from various cities, victories are rare. Therefore, Luno's victory or defeat cannot be judged solely on strength; it depends entirely on home advantage and local support. With all these rumors, this match was sure to be a good show, and the battle situation was certainly worth watching. Therefore, spectators of various nationalities from Bandung and neighboring cities enthusiastically came to see what was sure to be a rare event.

Teams Line Up, Testing the Waters First

At 4:25, the South China team, led by Captain Bao, entered the field. The whole team was full of energy and vitality, testing the waters. At 4:30, the Luno team also entered the field, radiating a murderous aura, as if they were prepared to die on the battlefield rather than lose their territory. They also briefly tested the waters. Then, Mr. Zeng Yingzhang, representing the organizing committee, presented a wreath, followed by Mr. Zheng Yuanquan, representing the Bandung Football Association, and Mr. Chen Zehe, representing the Youth Association, each presenting a wreath. Then, they chose their positions and deployed their formations.

The formations of the two sides were as follows:

South China Formation

Liang Yanzan, Ye Beihua, Li Tiansheng, Li Huitang

Bao Jiaping, Huang Meishun, Feng Jingxiang, Tan Jiangbai

Zhu Guolun, Liang Rongzhao, Zheng Shaokang

Luno Formation

Lajia Sha, He Sen, He Duoluo, Yu Dousi

Fan Le Ke, Bai Shengna, Daerma, Wu Hongsi

Sierya, Ximen, Helala

Equal Shares, Each Side Wins One

After the lines were set, Zeng Yingzhang entered the field to perform the opening ceremony. The silver whistle blew...

The intense battle began. Feng Jingxiang took the lead, leading his troops to attack. The enemy also launched a major counterattack with great momentum. Fortunately, the two defenders were strong and well-positioned, repelling everything. They then gained a free kick on the right side of the midfield. Li Tiansheng shot directly at the goal. The shot was excellent, hitting the post and bouncing out. Ye Beihua followed up, sweeping the ball diagonally out of the field. The effort failed. Ye Beihua's failure led to trouble. Luno's forces suddenly surged, creating a deafening momentum. The right winger dribbled straight in. South China's two defenders could not stop him, and he was overtaken by the enemy's left midfielder. Seeing the situation was not good, goalkeeper Bao went out to meet the attack, but it backfired. The enemy's left midfielder bypassed the two defenders and, seeing that the goalkeeper had come out, sent the ball into the net with a smooth kick. 1-0. Before Luno's joy could subside, South China had already led a large force to retaliate. Left midfielder Liang Yanzan intercepted the enemy's ball and dribbled it up the field, passing it to the flank. General Zheng received the ball, took a few steps, and then fiercely passed it inside. The ball landed right in the goal area. Ye Beihua chased after it, leaping up and heading the ball straight into the net like lightning, breaking the enemy's "egg" and creating a tie. 1-1. Local News

Anti-Japanese Aid to Overseas Chinese Conference Held Yesterday

Resolved on Four Measures to Eliminate Japanese Goods

Elected Yu Qiaqing as Chairman of the Committee

Chamber of Commerce Sends Telegram to Automatically Boycott Japanese Goods

Raising Large Sums to Aid Overseas Chinese in Korea

The Shanghai Anti-Japanese Aid to Overseas Chinese Committee held its first committee meeting yesterday afternoon, resolving measures to eliminate Japanese goods and deciding to telegraph the nation to raise relief funds. At the same time, seven standing committee members were elected, with Yu Qiaqing serving as chairman of the committee. In addition, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce held an executive committee meeting yesterday, passing a resolution to telegraph national chambers of commerce to automatically sever economic ties with Japan and halt the purchase of Japanese goods. Another telegram was sent to domestic and overseas chambers of commerce to raise large sums to aid overseas Chinese in Korea. Details of each item are recorded below:

Anti-Japanese Aid to Overseas Chinese Committee

The Shanghai All Circles Anti-Japanese Aid to Overseas Chinese Committee was convened yesterday by conveners Wang Xiaolai, Tao Baichuan, and Hou Dachun, inviting all committee members to hold the first committee meeting in the Municipal Chamber of Commerce's standing meeting room to discuss all ongoing matters. The meeting is recorded in detail below:

Committee Members Present: Wang Xiaolai, Wang Yansong, Yu Qiaqing, Ye Huijun, Deng Chengqing, Tao Baichuan, Yan Esheng, Chen Tingrui, Wang Wenhua, Li Yongxiang, Chen Peide, Hu Fengxiang, Chen Songyuan, Zhang Huijun, Wang Hanliang, Fang Jiaobo, Li Wenjie, Zhou Xuexiang, Liu Shimu, Xi Yushu, Lin Kecong, Wang Zhuping, Yu Hualong, Zhang Yichen, Feng Yixian, Cheng Zhusun, Li Cishan, Lu Jingshi, Lu Xingzhuang, Chen Ya'fu, Tang Junsheng, and over thirty others. After formal greetings, Wang Xiaolai was publicly elected as chairman, and Xue Guangqian as recorder.

Resolutions Passed: Next, the following resolutions were discussed and passed: (1) Appoint a committee to draft the organizational outline of this committee. Resolved to appoint Yan Esheng, Tao Baichuan, and Wang Yansong as drafting committee members. (2) How should the executive body of this committee be organized? Resolved to organize a standing committee of seven members, namely Wang Xiaolai, Wang Yansong, Tao Baichuan, Yu Qiaqing, Hou Dachun, Chen Tingrui, and Lu Jingshi. (3) How should the supervisory body of this committee be organized? Resolved to organize a supervisory committee and submit the list of candidates to the Municipal Party Headquarters for appointment. (4) Should this committee establish special committees? Resolved to first establish an economic committee of seven members, appointing Qin Runqing, Chen Guangfu, Zhang Gongquan, Xu Jimiao, Qian Xinzhi, and Xi Yushu. One additional member will be nominated by the standing committee members. The organizational charter will be drafted by the drafting committee. (5) How should the afflicted overseas Chinese be aided? Resolved: (A) Telegraph domestic and overseas organizations to donate relief funds, designating the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Shanghai Bank, Bank of China, Bank of Communications, National Industrial Bank of China, Central Bank of China, Four Banks Savings Society, and Fuyuan Exchange as collection agencies. (B) Petition the National Government to allocate one million yuan and send personnel to provide relief. (6) How should the anti-Japanese policy be carried out? Resolved to organize a design committee, with the selection of personnel and organization to be handled by the standing committee. (7) Set a date to hold a memorial service for the deceased overseas Chinese and to hold a supplementary oath-taking ceremony for the committee members. Resolved to hold a city-wide memorial service on July 23, with businesses closing for half a day in the morning and all hanging flags at half-mast to express condolences. (8) Should a work plan and implementation plan for this committee be drafted? Resolved to be handled by the standing committee. (9) Resolution on the outline for boycotting Japanese goods: (A) Promptly return goods that have already been ordered. (B) Stop shipping goods that have been ordered but have not yet arrived at the port. (C) Do not pick up goods that are stored in warehouses but have not been paid for. (D) Goods that have already been purchased must first be registered with the committee and temporarily suspended from sale. Those who violate the above four measures will be

dealt with severely in accordance with the prescribed disciplinary regulations. (10) How should this committee be organized? Resolved to establish a chairman and secretary, as well as six sections: general affairs, publicity, inspection, investigation, registration, and storage. Appoint Yu Qiaqing as chairman, Yan Esheng as secretary, Wang Xiaolai concurrently as director of the general affairs section, Tao Baichuan concurrently as director of the publicity section, Hou Dachun concurrently as director of the inspection section, Lu Jingshi concurrently as director of the investigation section, Chen Tingrui concurrently as director of the registration section, and Wang Yansong concurrently as director of the storage section. Each section will have one deputy director, to be appointed from the committee members, to be decided at the next meeting. (11) Should this committee formulate reward and punishment regulations? Resolved to appoint Fang Jiaobo, Hou Dachun, and Feng Yixian to draft the regulations. (12) On what date should this committee officially begin operations? Resolved to begin operations immediately. (13) What should be the address of this committee? Resolved to use the former Tianhou Palace Temple as the committee's address. (14) Should the committee's seal be made? Resolved to make a seal with the inscription [Seal of the Shanghai All Circles Anti-Japanese Aid to Overseas Chinese Committee]. (15) Set the date for the committee's regular meetings. Resolved to hold meetings once a week at 5:00 PM.

Shanghai Chamber of Commerce

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce held its 17th Executive Committee meeting yesterday at 4 PM. Wang Xiaolai, Wang Yansong, Xu Jigu, Fang Jiaobo, Zhu Wenqi, Wu Zhihao, Ye Huijun, Chen Songyuan, Wen Lanting, Jiang Zhigang, and over ten others resolved the following matters: (1) Send a telegram to chambers of commerce at home and abroad to raise funds to assist Chinese nationals in Korea who have suffered; (2) Send a telegram to all chambers of commerce nationwide to lead merchants in a systematic organization for voluntary economic severance with Japan; (3) Convene a special members' meeting on the 24th of this month to discuss practical measures for implementing economic severance with Japan; (4) Send a letter requesting Wang Yansong not to resign as a supervisor of the Municipal Party Headquarters. The following official documents and notices have been communicated:

Telegram 1 To: Singapore, Penang, Australia, Canada, America, Sydney, Victoria, New York, San Francisco, Philippines, Honolulu, Southern Vietnam, Batavia, Surabaya, Siam, Chinese Chambers of Commerce: Since the 4th, Chinese nationals in various parts of Korea have been persecuted by Korean mobs. For several days, thousands have been killed or injured, and over ten thousand have lost their jobs and are returning home. Without relief, Chinese commerce in Korea will be utterly destroyed. Our Chamber has initiated fundraising, but we fear our resources are insufficient. Your compatriots reside in foreign lands and have experienced many hardships. Upon hearing this terrible news, we feel the pain as if it were our own. Please provide vigorous assistance, collect a substantial sum, and remit it to our Chamber at any time for transfer. Shanghai Chamber of Commerce.

Telegram 2 To: All Chambers of Commerce Nationwide: The severe and tragic situation of the persecution of Chinese nationals by Koreans instigated by the Japanese has been reported in the newspapers daily. The Japanese claim that the unrest has been quelled, but the vegetable gardens of Chinese farmers have been completely destroyed, and the goods of self-employed merchants have been looted. Even summer cloth about to be marketed has been left unable to be traded due to the destruction of the Chinese merchants' foundations. Only export has been stopped. Judging from the continuous return of Chinese nationals from Yantai to the mainland in recent days, with over a thousand people each time, it is evident that this Japanese conspiracy is using Koreans to act swiftly and decisively, eradicating the decades of hard-won Chinese commerce in Korea to achieve their economic annexation plan. The so-called "unrest has been quelled" is merely a euphemism for nothing left to destroy or loot, the goal having been achieved. Chinese merchants in Korea have historically and emotionally held a superior position compared to other countries. Since the annexation of Korea by Japan, the Japanese have repeatedly increased tariffs in an attempt to force them out. However, due to the Chinese's diligence and Koreans' reliance on the Chinese, the deep-rooted economic relationship of the Chinese over the decades has not been easily uprooted. Therefore, they have resorted to sowing discord and inciting ignorant Koreans to be their tools of murder. First, there was the anti-Chinese incident in 1927, followed by the current large-scale joint riots in various places, demonstrating a consistent policy containing international conspiracy. Although Chinese nationals in Korea come from all provinces, Shandong accounts for the majority. Shandong people who go abroad to make a living are found throughout Russian Siberia in the north and the eight provinces of Korea in the east, numbering hundreds of thousands. This helps to regulate the densely populated area, similar to how the southern diaspora of Fujian and Guangdong provinces relies on the Nanyang Islands. Since Russia implemented Soviet policies, all commerce has been nationalized, and Chinese nationals have no place to stand there. The only area they rely on for foreign development is this corner of the Korean peninsula. If they suffer unexpected adversity again and submit to fate without seeking rescue, it will be seen that our country's commerce with Korea will decline, and Shandong's surplus population will have no place to migrate to. Its impact on the future of the nation is significant and should not be viewed as a local disaster to be ignored. Therefore, planning for the aftermath of the Chinese nationals is to provide full assistance from the entire nation, regardless of whether they have returned home or not, so that they can reorganize their assets and restore their old businesses, so as not to be defeated and allow the Japanese conspiracy to succeed. The areas where Chinese nationals have been harmed this time, such as Pyongyang, Incheon, and Seoul, are all important cities or commercial centers. The losses are likely to exceed ten million. Although our Chamber has launched a fundraising campaign to help Chinese nationals, the purpose of this assistance is not for temporary relief but for business recovery. Therefore, it is not enough to call on all the magnates to raise large sums of money for coping. Therefore, the 17th Executive Committee meeting of our Chamber decided to telegraph to various chambers of commerce to voluntarily initiate a sustained and effective economic severance with Japan and to unanimously assist in collecting funds to help the Chinese nationals who have been harmed in Korea. Please record the case and convey the telegram, hoping that your esteemed association will enthusiastically support it with the heart of rescuing those in peril, start fundraising immediately, and remit the collected amount to our Chamber at any time for transfer or directly to the Chinese Chambers of Commerce in Korea. Shanghai Chamber of Commerce.

Telegram 3 To: All Chambers of Commerce Nationwide: Regarding the Japanese instigation of Koreans to persecute Chinese nationals, our Chamber has resolved to telegraph for fundraising assistance and to automatically lead the business community in economic severance with Japan. The case has already been telegraphed separately. Economic severance with Japan has been held repeatedly in recent years, but each time, various sectors have led in front and merchants have followed behind. In terms of its previous effects, the following two drawbacks are unavoidable: (1) Since the leaders are from various sectors, they cannot fully understand the actual situation of the goods, so there are often cases of mistaken detention and fines. Even if the matter is repeatedly appealed and clarified, the merchant's unexpected losses are uncountable. (2) Since there are mistaken detentions and fines, one party is busy appealing, which inevitably diverts their energy for external affairs, and the actual work of economic severance is inevitably relaxed. Moreover, merchants who have been mistakenly detained and fined are inevitably discouraged and lose their faith, resulting in their inability to resist for a long time. Summarizing the above two points, merchants cannot automatically take action for economic severance, and they themselves suffer endless pain, and resistance is difficult to achieve thoroughly, which makes the ambitious laugh from the sidelines and adds another humiliation to the national shame. Past economic severance failures are deeply painful. The motives for economic severance have mostly arisen from foreign political aggression, but this time it stems purely from economic aggression. What they want to destroy is the commercial status of Chinese nationals in Korea. Therefore, those who are killed are merchants, those who are destroyed are shops, and those who are looted are goods. If they are trying to eliminate our merchants as their goal, and we turn to begging for their leftovers and relying on Japanese goods to survive, how can we not be insane to come to this? Therefore, today, whether it is for the sake of national survival, national dignity, or the interests of the merchants themselves, at this moment when the hideous face of economic aggression is fully exposed, merchants must rise up and take the initiative to direct the final victory. Otherwise, the suffering and humiliation will be tenfold more than today. Your esteemed association is a leader in the business community. If you accept these humble views, please convene all merchants to form a systematic organization for voluntary economic severance with Japan, so that this economic severance with Japan can fully exert its effectiveness, wash away the accumulated habits of starting but never finishing, not only for the glory of the nation but also to create an unprecedented record in the business community. Shanghai Chamber of Commerce.

Notice 1 The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce urgently notified various trade associations yesterday, saying: We are forwarding a telegram from the Provisional Presidium of the Anti-Japanese Aid-Korea Grand Assembly of Various Circles in this city, stating (already seen in yesterday's newspaper, omitted) etc. The tragic massacre of overseas Chinese is a common indignation of the whole country. Stopping the import of Japanese goods and economic severance with Japan is the only way to deal with it. Please record the telegram and forward it to your industry colleagues for earnest implementation.

Notice 2 The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce issued an urgent notice regarding the cancellation of the organization of a delegation to Japan to investigate the Wanbaoshan and Korean Chinese victims cases, saying: In view of the fact that the Japanese have repeatedly organized inspection groups to come to China amid the worldwide economic downturn, and the new treaty between the two countries based on international equality is being negotiated by the government, the relationship between China and Japan in commerce may be opened in another way. The Chamber is canceling the aforementioned proposal for a commercial inspection group to Japan from this day forward, and hereby publishes this notice.

Expressions from All Sides

Yu Qiaqing's Statement: Since the Anti-Japanese Aid-Korea Grand Assembly of Various Circles implemented economic severance with Japan, Japanese merchants in Shanghai have been panicking. The Japanese Consul recently (the 16th) sent Vice Consul Shirai Yasushi, a member of the House of Representatives, Kato Taiichi, to visit the commercial leaders of the Anti-Japanese Aid-Korea Committee, Yu Qiaqing, to state that Ambassador Shigemitsu had gone to Nanjing to meet with Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting to negotiate a settlement and that there would be a solution. Yu replied that the first step in this action against Japan was to stop ordering Japanese goods, the second step was to boycott Japanese goods, and the third step was to implement economic severance with Japan. Now it is still in the preliminary stage. If the Japanese authorities can realize this and find a satisfactory solution, then it may be possible to negotiate, otherwise the people should proceed with the second and third steps. Then they returned without getting what they wanted.

Statements from Industry and Commerce: The Shanghai Silk-Mercerized Cotton Weaving Industry Association held a special members' meeting yesterday. Chairman Zhu Wenqi reported on the Wanbaoshan massacre. All members were extremely indignant and decided to automatically boycott enemy goods and submit concrete proposals to the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Dyeing and Weaving Industry Federation for a unified approach. Pawnshops, laundries, leather shoe nailing and last-making industries, knitting industries, etc., as well as the Seamen's Branch, the Naval Special Party Department, etc., all sent telegrams yesterday to express their indignation.

Shipping News Amidst the Boycott

Japanese Goods Rushed to Shanghai: Since the incident in Korea, various circles in Shanghai have proposed economic severance with Japan, which is already in progress. Japanese people in Shanghai, hearing the news that goods ordered but not yet shipped to Shanghai may be blocked, telegraphed the Toyo Kisen Kaisha on the 14th to quickly load the large quantities of goods they had ordered and ship them to Shanghai. It has been agreed that the Japanese Post Office will send eleven ships to transport them. In addition, Yamashita, Kawasaki, Mitsui, and others have also temporarily dispatched a large number of merchant ships to Kobe and Yokohama to transport goods continuously. The first batch has already arrived in Shanghai, and they plan to send more ships before the boycott is formally launched. Yesterday, the Japanese Post Office specially convened Japanese merchants in Shanghai to discuss plans to expedite the loading. Large quantities of Japanese goods will arrive in Shanghai one after another and then be transferred to other ports.

Foreign Ships Used to Ship Goods: The warehouses of Japanese shipping companies in Shanghai, such as Huishan, Osaka, and Pudong, have the most goods stored, mostly sugar, seafood, paper, and cloth. From the 14th, the Japanese merchants negotiated with Nisshin, Osaka, Dalian, and Butterfield & Swire, and other foreign shipping companies to reserve cargo tonnage, shipping the goods stored in Shanghai warehouses within one week. About 70-80% of these goods were destined for the Yangtze River. The foreign ships, partly because of their national ties (Japanese ships) and partly because of business relations, have agreed. Therefore, foreign merchants' Yangtze River cargo exports have been crowded in the past three days and are being shipped urgently.

Preventing Smuggling to Various Ports: The Customs Brokers Association has learned that Japan has decided on a secret loading plan for cargo transportation. According to this plan, goods from Japan to Shanghai will be handled by Japanese customs brokers, who will only load them onto Japanese and British ships for export to the Yangtze River and the northern and southern oceans, but not onto Chinese merchant ships. This measure is to avoid the boycott, etc. Yu Senting, a director of the Customs Brokers Association, visited Yu Qiaqing yesterday to discuss with the Jianghai Customs to request them to report secretly on the arrival of Japanese goods and to refuse customs declarations for foreign ships to prevent the cunning scheme from succeeding.

Chinese Ships Do Not Load Japanese Goods: Since the decision not to load Japanese goods has not yet been formally discussed, various Chinese shipping companies have not yet received any notice from any organization. However, out of conscience, various Chinese ships in Shanghai have automatically stopped loading Japanese goods, but this is an informal act.

Yesterday

Pilot Full Strike

Foreign Ships Blocked at Wusong Estuary

If Insistence on No Return to Work Continues

Customs Plans to Use Chinese Staff

The Foreign Ship Pilots Association has been on strike because their request for increased fees was rejected by the shipping companies. As of yesterday, they were on full strike. Ships coming to Shanghai from foreign countries were either blocked at Tongsha Lianghe Cave or arrived at Wusong but could not enter the port, and traffic has been completely halted. Yesterday, many ships coming to Shanghai on their own exported on their own without using pilots. The shipping companies met yesterday morning at the association to discuss rescue measures, but there was no hope of a solution. The content was kept highly confidential. After much inquiry by our reporter, it was learned that, according to the River Conservancy Department, in the event that the pilots insist, the shipping companies will decide to replace them with Chinese pilots in order to maintain maritime transport. The following is a detailed account of the information obtained:

Foreign Ships Cannot Enter: The starting point of the pilot line is Lianghe Cave outside Tongsha in Wusong, about four hours by sea from Shanghai. The most difficult part is the first section of Tongsha River. The pilot ship is stationed at Lianghe Cave, and the pilot comes to Shanghai. Since the shipping companies did not agree to increase the fees, all pilots have stopped work since yesterday, causing ships coming from Europe and the United States to stop at Tongsha and unable to enter the Huangpu River. The French postal ship D'Artagnan, a regular mail ship that could not be delayed, was piloted by the captain himself and also exported without using a pilot. Cargoes of other ships that have been blocked cannot arrive in Shanghai for unloading and are waiting for the matter to be resolved.

Meeting Unfruitful: The various shipping companies sent representatives to the association at 9:00 AM yesterday to hold a general meeting to discuss the matter. Representatives from European and American ships all attended the meeting to negotiate for a long time, and they did not want to announce the content. However, it was heard that there was no result under negotiation because the pilots were unwilling to give in. A temporary plan has been discussed regarding rescue measures.

Proposal to Employ Chinese Staff: The pilot strike

Page 14

has lasted three days since the 15th and there is still no hope of returning to work. Shanghai is an international trade center, and the daily traffic of merchants and passengers from all countries is as usual. If this continues, maritime traffic will also be cut off. The River Conservancy Department of Jianghai Customs believes that there is no factual reason to increase fees. If they do not return to work, in order to maintain Shanghai's maritime traffic and international trade, the striking pilots will be suspended from their duties and the Customs will rehire Chinese staff from the Yangtze River Pilot Association. (Note: There are two pilot associations in Shanghai, one is the Foreign Merchant Pilot Association, which specializes in piloting foreign ships to Shanghai and currently has more than 30 people. There is only one Chinese, Mr. Zhang). The other is the Yangtze River Pilot Association, which is organized by Chinese pilots and is responsible for guiding the Yangtze River ships of various companies, which can avoid foreign ships being blocked at the Wusong estuary. Yesterday, the various shipping companies unanimously expressed their sympathy for this proposal. According to the state's planned measures, the implementation of recovering the foreign pilots' rights in Shanghai has been agreed upon by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, etc., to be completed by the end of 1933. From New Year's Day 1934, foreign pilots will be withdrawn from all parts of the country and replaced by Chinese pilots. The Navy is currently training this talent.

Municipal Public Security Bureau

Dismantled Reactionary Organization

Confiscated Two Radios

Many Reactionary Criminals from Shanxi

A large number of reactionary elements were arrested in the French Concession. The details are as follows: The Municipal Public Security Bureau received a secret report that Yan Xishan had recently sent a large number of personnel to Shanghai to plot to disrupt the rear and attempt to achieve his goals, and to communicate with reactionary factions from all sides. Based on the report, Director Chen secretly ordered the Detective Captain to lead detectives and plainclothes officers to cooperate with the French Concession police detectives to rush to No. 208 Saposai Road, No. 13 Messer de Dillon Road, and a certain tannery in the western part of Shanghai, where more than ten Shanxi reactionary criminals, including Tian Yunqing, were arrested, and two radios, a secret telegraph codebook, and a volume of secret telegraph drafts were seized. A list of Shanghai military addresses and multiple entry and exit permits for welcoming Yan were found. The French police detectives took the suspects and evidence to the police station for interrogation. The Municipal Public Security Bureau is negotiating extradition. It is regrettable that when the arrest was made, two important criminals escaped because someone had tipped them off in advance.

Zhu Yingpeng Resigns from Party Committee Position

Reorganizing China Public School

No Time to Attend to Party Affairs

Mr. Zhu Yingpeng, Secretary-General and Director of General Affairs of China Public School, has served two terms as a member of the Municipal Party Committee. Mr. Zhu is currently in charge of reorganizing China Public School, and he has no time to attend to party affairs. He previously went to Nanjing to explain the situation to the Central Committee and requested to resign, but his request was not approved. After the new Municipal Committee was announced, Mr. Zhu again submitted a resignation. The original petition stated that he has been serving in the journalism industry for many years and it is difficult to leave suddenly. Since he was appointed by the Ministry of Education this spring to take over China Public School, he is still working in the school after the reorganization. The affairs are both troublesome and lacking in spare time to attend to party affairs. Therefore, he specially requests to resign in order to concentrate on education, which is also serving the party indirectly.

US Consul General Responds to Taxpayer Association's Letter

Extremely Sorry for Unfortunate Incident

The Shanghai Public Concession Chinese Taxpayers' Association received a letter from the US Consul General yesterday, stating: "I have received your letter of June 4 of this year, in which you stated that certain unfortunate incidents have recently occurred between our nationals and Chinese residents in this city, and requested that I investigate. The purpose of your association's letter to request the attention of this Consul General on such cases is respected by this Consul General. As for the request to emphasize the friendly relations between China and the United States and to resolve these cases satisfactorily, this Consul General has also paid attention to it. This Consul General deeply regrets the occurrence of such misunderstandings between the people of your country and my country, and will do his best to eliminate them. This is something that your association can believe in without worry. Regarding the Gu Jingen shooting case and the case of Qu Shixiang and Ma Ruixiang being harmed by US sailors, I am pleased to forward a copy of the letter sent to the Mayor of Shanghai today for your review. The letter details the US Navy Commander's solution to the case. As for the case of Dai Tingzuo accidentally drowning, the testimonies were contradictory, so it is impossible to ascertain exactly what happened at the time and the cause of the person's fall into the water. However, in order to comfort the peddler's father, a compensation of two hundred and fifty yuan was given to the US sailor who was present at the drowning. This case is closed. This office has not heard of the stabbing of Yang Jin'er, Sun Debao, Wang Jinfa, Ma Lin, etc. at Qichang Store. This case has not been reported to this office by the parties concerned or the Chinese authorities. If your association provides all the information, this Consul General will immediately order an investigation. In the letter from this Consul General to the Mayor, there is a sentence that reads, "This Consul General is extremely sorry for the unfortunate occurrence of the incident in the letter." It is hoped that your association will review it. One more point that this Consul General would like your association to pay attention to is that if such cases are submitted to the appropriate court to determine the guilt of the parties concerned, many misunderstandings can be avoided. Chinese and American people are willing to be good citizens who abide by the law. Therefore, whenever misunderstandings occur, the best thing to do is to resort to the mechanisms established by the two governments to resolve disputes according to law, rather than publishing harsh words in the newspapers of this city. This method of announcement does not help to resolve the case, but harms the existing cordial relations between the two countries."

The contents of the letter replying to Mayor Zhang are briefly as follows: The case of Qu Shixiang and Ma Ruixiang has been publicly tried by a special military court organized by the US Navy Commander. It is reported that the Anhui Association also had representatives present to listen. The Chinese judge in the Gu Jingen case believes that the US sailor fired in self-defense, but if Gu Jingen's brother is not satisfied, he can appeal to the US Attorney's Office, which will be able to make a fair judgment.

International Trade Bureau

Officially Established on August 1

The Ministry of Industry Has Appointed Guo Bingwen as Director

The Bureau of Industrial and Commercial Visits Will Be Abolished After Establishment

The Ministry of Industry previously ordered Guo Bingwen, Director of the Bureau of Industrial and Commercial Visits, on February 24 to start preparations for the International Trade Bureau. The organizational regulations have been submitted to the Ministry for revision and then submitted to the Executive Yuan for submission to the National Government. The Legislative Yuan has now passed it, and the detailed rules of procedure have also been drafted by the Ministry of Industry. It is scheduled to be officially established in Shanghai on August 1, and Guo Bingwen has been appointed as the director. The internal four departments, including taxation, guidance, statistics, and compilation, have a monthly budget of 20,000 yuan. Its mission is to promote and guide international trade. After the official establishment, the Bureau of Industrial and Commercial Visits will be abolished. The candidates for the deputy director and the four department heads have not yet been announced. It is likely that they will be former members of the Bureau of Industrial and Commercial Visits. A reporter from the Xinsheng News Agency visited Guo Bingwen yesterday and was received by Secretary Zhao Shutong, who said that the Bureau has not yet received the order to abolish it. The order to establish the International Trade Bureau next month and Guo's letter of appointment will probably be received within days.

Port Quarantine Office Replies to Shipping Association's Letter

Regarding Shanghai-Ningbo Ship Quarantine

The Port Quarantine Office has received reports from various parties that there have been cholera symptoms found in the city recently, and it is deeply feared that the disease will be transmitted to the interior. Therefore, it is planned to start with the quarantine of ships coming from Ningbo. The various Chinese and foreign shipping companies have been notified accordingly. The Taikoo and Jardine companies immediately complied and replied, while the various Chinese companies have mostly used

excuses to obstruct it. This matter is of great importance and must be carried out. Chinese merchants may not fully understand quarantine matters, resulting in deep

suspicion. Therefore, a letter was specially sent to the Shipping Association to explain. The original letter is excerpted below: In response to your letter of the 15th, saying [briefly, that the inspection of ships coming from Ningbo and the injection of cholera vaccine hinder traffic and affect business, etc.], the importance of quarantine has long been recognized internationally. It is only because the government decree is newly created that those who are ignorant may not fully understand it, so once the epidemic spreads, they run around in panic and do not know what to do, which is lamentable. Since the establishment of this office, the work of quarantining, exterminating rats, and fumigating ships for foreign ships has been convenient for everyone, and there is no such situation as described in the letter. According to quarantine regulations, reports must be made to the office 24 hours before the ship enters the port, and quarantine procedures must be carried out in the port. In order to facilitate merchants and travelers, it is only necessary for the medical officer to board the ship at the port and carry out quarantine and vaccination procedures along the way. When the ship is docked, it will be completed, ensuring that there will be no disturbance or obstruction of business. It is not necessary for everyone to be vaccinated, as described in the letter, and there are no fees or various difficult procedures. The country seeks happiness for the health of the people and seeks cooperation for the national health with the League of Nations. The establishment of official epidemic prevention is very different from other institutions. According to the report of the Public Concession Public Works Bureau doctor, cholera symptoms were found in Shanghai on the 9th of this month. If early prevention is not taken, the spread is worrying. It is appropriate for our Chinese shipping industry to share this understanding and assist in carrying out the epidemic prevention policy. Chairman Su and the committee members are highly respected and knowledgeable, and they are admired by the public. They are particularly enthusiastic in advocating for important policies for the welfare of the people. It is hoped that you will forward the letter to explain that there will be no more excuses to obstruct the promotion of the epidemic prevention policy.

News of China Merchant Steam Navigation Company Vessels Delayed by Flooding

Offshore: In the past week, a sudden flood occurred upstream in the Baihe River in Tianjin. The rushing water carried sand and mud downstream, causing the Baihe River to become severely silted up and shallow. Vessels with drafts of six feet or more are now unable to enter Tanggu, and both cargo and passengers must be transferred at Dagu. Various shipping companies in Shanghai have agreed to add a transfer fee of 1.68 taels per ton for goods destined for Tianjin, starting from the 19th. Therefore, the Ningbo and Shanghai merchants have been rushing to transport goods to Tianjin in recent days. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, due to the large volume of goods and the shortage of ships going to Tianjin, has also changed the routes of the "Nanhua" and "Yuanan" vessels to serve the Tianjin route.

Inland Rivers: Small steamboats on the inland rivers of Jiangsu and Zhejiang have been stopped by floods in various locations. Routes such as the Shanghai-Wuxi, Shanghai-Changzhou, Shanghai-Huzhou, and Jiaxing lines have all suspended operations for a week. Recently, the weather has cleared, and although water has been drained from the fields, the river levels have not receded. The Shanghai-Huzhou night service has resumed, and the daytime service resumed trial operations yesterday. The Wuxi line, due to the gradual receding of waters between Kunshan and Bacheng, resumed cargo services yesterday at the request of the business community. However, passenger services have not resumed, and the service will operate as a "slow train." The Changshu line is expected to resume operations in two or three days. Currently, inland river vessels are gradually resuming service, with only the Shanghai-Changzhou line remaining closed.

Recent News from the Committee Opposing American Soldiers' Atrocities

The Shanghai All-Circles Committee Opposing the Atrocities of American Sailors sent representatives Zhu Ping'an and Zhao Shusheng to the Diplomatic Representative Office in Shanghai the day before yesterday to submit a letter to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and a letter to the Diplomatic Discussion Committee. Zhao Tiezhang of the Representative Office accepted and forwarded the letters. The submitted letters are extracted as follows: (1) A letter to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs: Regarding the barbarous atrocities of American soldiers, harming our compatriots, earnestly requesting a swift and severe protest to the American government, demanding punishment of the perpetrators, an apology, and compensation, and promptly and voluntarily recovering the concessions and extraterritorial rights to fundamentally resolve the situation and protect the lives of the people and the integrity of the nation. Since two months ago, American soldiers stationed in Shanghai have repeatedly used firearms to kill Gu Jingen, stab Qu Shixiang, Ma Ruixiang, and push Dai Tingzuo into the river to their death. Furthermore, American sailors in Qichang Pier in Pudong wielded weapons and injured Yang Jin'er, Wang Jinfa, Ma Lin, and Sun Debao. The news of these atrocities has enraged all of our countrymen. What have our people done to deserve such cruelty? In addition to demanding punishment of the perpetrators, an apology, and compensation for all losses, we request that your Ministry make every effort to negotiate to achieve these goals. As for the issues of concessions and consular jurisdiction, they are the shields for the unbridled behavior of American sailors. We urge your Ministry to abide by the resolutions of the National Assembly and strive to recover the concessions and extraterritorial rights in the shortest possible time. Our committee, together with all the citizens of Shanghai, will wholeheartedly support this effort. We urgently request your review and guidance on how to proceed, and we ask for your instructions with the utmost anticipation. (2) A letter to the Diplomatic Discussion Committee: Respectfully informing you that since two months ago, American soldiers and civilians have arbitrarily infringed upon the lives of our compatriots within our country's territory. The first incident was the case of American sailors shooting and killing Gu Jingen on April 24. The second incident was the case of American sailors stabbing Qu Shixiang and Ma Ruixiang. The third incident was the case of American sailors pushing Dai Tingzuo into the river to their death. The fourth incident was the case of American sailors stabbing Yang Jin'er, Sun Debao, Wang Jinfa, and Ma Lin. Such tragic incidents have occurred repeatedly. If we do not arouse public outrage and lodge a strong protest, future disasters will be even more imminent, and our people will have no peace. Our committee was formed by various circles in Shanghai and is now actively proceeding. We have always admired your committee as a pioneer in diplomacy. We dare to send you a letter detailing the situation and request that your committee raise it for discussion and provide guidance to facilitate our progress. We eagerly await your response.

Record of the Opening of the Fishing Vessel Crew Training Session

A Pioneering Initiative in China's Fishing Industry

The Jiangsu Provincial Fisheries Experimental Field, in light of the fact that foreign fishing vessels have been invading our coastal waters for over ten thousand yuan annually, and that our domestic fishing technology lags behind, has taken advantage of the summer ship repair and fishing moratorium period for various Chinese fishing vessels in Shanghai. They held the first session of the Summer Training Program for Fishing Vessel Crews at the Yucai School at Dadongmen, providing technical and academic guidance. This event is a pioneering initiative in China. The opening ceremony was held at 5:00 PM on the 16th. The chairman was Wang Wentai, the director of the field, and the master of ceremonies and recorder was Wang Liansheng. Attendees included senior crew members such as captains, engineers, and chief mates from various fishing vessels including Haixing, Yongmao, Lianfeng, Zhenning, and Jimei; Hou Chaohai and Chen Moulang, representatives from the Agricultural and Mining Department of Jiangsu Province; Yang Shuheng, captain of the Fuhai warship; fisheries experts Chen Zhunian and Zhang Junfeng; Wu and Li, representatives from the Zhejiang fresh fish merchants; Chen Shuyi, technician and captain of the experimental field; Zhang Zhuzun, technical director; Wang Liansheng, a member of the preparatory committee for the Provincial Fisheries Guidance Institute; Mao Jusheng, a fisheries correspondent; and employees from various fishing vessel companies, totaling over 50 people. The ceremony proceeded according to protocol. First, Chairman Wang Wentai reported the purpose of the meeting and compared trawl fishing industries in China and abroad. He expressed the hope that people would not be satisfied with the current situation and must strive for progress. He stated that although the planning for this event was not entirely complete, the professors hired were all fisheries experts, and the various charts and diagrams were made to ensure that the attending crew members fully understood them. It is also planned to continue holding various classified fisheries training sessions in the future so that our fishing vessel crews can fully acquire research opportunities. Next, Hou Chaohai, the representative from the Agricultural and Mining Department, gave a speech stating that the province's fisheries administration is divided into four types: (1) experimentation, (2) investigation, (3) guidance, and (4) research. Training sessions for crew members should be divided into three types: fishing vessel crew members, engine room personnel, and others related to the fisheries industry. Future training sessions should also be planned for those related to the fisheries industry, such as personnel from fisheries groups and cooperatives. Finally, he hoped that the attendees would pay more attention to literacy and transportation. Afterwards, the chairman reported on the types of courses and their outlines. The ceremony ended at 6:00 PM. Everyone had dinner, and then the first lesson of the class began at 6:30 PM. Chen Moulang lectured on the doctrine of the Party, and Wang Wentai lectured on the general situation of the trawl fishing industry. The lecture ended at 8:30 PM. The attending crew members rarely have the opportunity to attend such training sessions because they work hard at sea all year round, so they were very focused and orderly throughout the session, which was commendable. All expenses required for the session were borne solely by the Jiangsu Provincial Fisheries Experimental Field. The training dates were from the 16th to the 31st, from 4:30 PM to 8:00 PM every afternoon. Dinner was provided for the attendees to save time. There were more than ten types of courses. In addition to lectures, Chinese and foreign fisheries films were screened from the 21st onwards to give attendees a sense of what was being discussed.

League of Nations Representatives Investigating Trafficking of Women and Children Depart Shanghai

Dr. and Mrs. Johnson, representatives of the League of Nations investigating the trafficking of women and children in the Far East, and their companions, returned to China from Japan a few days ago. After staying in Shanghai for two days, they departed Shanghai on the "President Coolidge" yesterday and headed to Southeast Asia. They will stay in Singapore for two or three weeks and then return to Europe on August 25, it is said.

Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs

Strictly Ordering All Labor Unions to Register According to Law

A One-Week Deadline Given

The Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs yesterday strictly ordered all labor unions in the city that have been established but have not yet registered according to law. It has been ordered that all labor unions established before June of this year that have not yet registered, having been previously notified by this bureau and the Public Training Committee of the City Party Headquarters in Announcement No. 3883 to apply for registration within a limited time, have now exceeded the deadline for many days, and there are still those who have neglected to comply. This is a disregard for the law. Therefore, in addition to issuing separate orders, this bureau urgently orders the relevant labor unions to comply and apply for registration according to law within one week from the date of this order. Any further delay will be deemed inappropriate. This order is of utmost importance.

Record of the Meeting of the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce National Goods Market

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce Merchandise Exhibition Hall National Goods Market convened its fourth committee meeting at 3:00 PM the day before yesterday. The attendees included Zhang Baoshan, Zhu Dechao, Xu Dianhuang, Wang Lisun, Pan Dechun, Pei Weimin, Yu Xingben, Xi Guansheng, Fang Chuangge, Ding Xunhao, and others, totaling 13 people. The chairman was Zhu Dechao, and the recorder was Zhong Yingnian. The resolutions were as follows: (1) Regarding whether the market should publish a catalog of product samples and prices, it was resolved that each factory should prepare and submit its own product samples and price catalogs. (2) Regarding the market's holidays, it was resolved that the market would follow the holiday schedule of major companies in Shanghai, except for Sundays. (3) Regarding the discount period, it was resolved that there would be a three-week discount period for each of the four seasons, spring, summer, autumn, and winter, and for the anniversary of the market's opening each week. The National Goods Promotion Week would have a one-week discount. The start dates would be based on the practices of major companies in Shanghai. (4) Regarding the sale of substandard goods, it was resolved that all factories participating in the market must not sell substandard goods. If substandard goods are found, they must be returned to the factory immediately. (5) Regarding the sale of mixed goods worth between one and five yuan, it was resolved that the office would prepare detailed measures when the second-floor market holds its opening and then discuss them further. (6) Regarding the exchange of silver dollars, it was resolved that the market would follow the posted rates of the local tobacco and exchange shops and announce them daily. (7) Provisional proposals: (1) It was resolved that the market's business hours would be from the same morning hours as before, but the evening hours would be shortened by half an hour to 8:30 PM, starting from August 1. (2) It was resolved that the discussion on advertising expenses would be postponed until September. (3) It was resolved that the market office would send another letter to the factory's general manager requesting that the name of the store manager be submitted to the market by a specific date.

Ying Chong Bank Business Report

For the Year 19

The 14th Annual General Meeting of Shareholders of Ying Chong Bank was held on June 27, 1931, in the Maaya Building on Tank Road, Singapore. The Board of Directors presented the business report and financial statements for 1930. After deducting depreciation on buildings and furniture, bad debts, and stationery expenses, and allocating 10% for bad debt reserves, the actual profit for the year was 542,892.18 Straits dollars (approximately 2.50 yuan in national currency per Straits dollar; the same applies below). Together with the 249,893.56 Straits dollars carried over from 1929, the total was 792,785.74 Straits dollars. The Board of Directors proposed the following allocation: (1) 14% dividend payment of 400,000 Straits dollars. (2) 100,000 Straits dollars allocated to the public reserve fund. (3) 10,000 Straits dollars for the Board of Directors' remuneration. (4) 282,785.74 Straits dollars carried forward to the next year's account, totaling 792,785.74 Straits dollars. The total capital of the bank is 20 million Straits dollars, with 8 million Straits dollars subscribed and 4 million Straits dollars fully paid. Shareholders also bear a guarantee liability of 4 million Straits dollars. The public reserve fund is 2,687,000 Straits dollars, it is said.

Establishment of the 22nd District Branch of the Citizens' Association

The Shanghai Special District Citizens' Association, 22nd District Branch, located in Jing'an Temple in western Shanghai, was initiated and organized by Xu Wenyuan, Wang Hancheng, Gong Yifei, Zhang Pinshan, Wu Binghua, Qin Linsheng, Chen Yusheng, Cai Jiugao, and others. Its establishment was approved by the City Party Headquarters, the Public Training Committee, and the Citizens' Association. Many nearby shops and residents have joined enthusiastically. Preparations are now complete, and the inaugural meeting is scheduled for 2:00 PM tomorrow at Jing'an Primary School in Jing'an Temple. Representatives from the City Party Headquarters, the Public Training Committee, the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs, and the Citizens' Association will attend to provide guidance and supervise the election of the executive committee. There will also be entertainment provided by various sectors to add to the festive atmosphere. It is expected to be a grand occasion.

Ding Shujing

A Report on Recent News from the Tianjin and Beiping YWCAs

Ms. Ding Shujing, General Secretary of the National Association of YWCAs, after returning to China from Europe and America, stayed in Shanghai for a short time and then went on a tour at the end of May, first to Hangzhou, then to Nanjing, Jinan, Tianjin, and Beiping, to observe the work of the YWCAs in various cities and discuss various plans with the directors and staff in those areas, as well as preparations for the third national conference next year and the YWCA World Conference to be held in China the year after. She has now completed her work and returned to Shanghai. According to Ms. Ding, the work of the various associations has made great progress, especially in Beiping and Tianjin, where there have been new developments. The Beiping YWCA, due to the presence of many schools in Beiping and the large number of students, especially female students from other provinces, has found that students from far away often find it inconvenient to find food and lodging. In order to make things easier for female students from various schools, the association has rented a building in Xiyuli Road and founded a dormitory and club for female students. The location is quiet, the building is spacious, and all modern amenities, such as running water, electricity, and telephones, are available. There are also various games and sports equipment available for after-class recreation. The opening ceremony was held on June 20. It is believed that female students from various schools will feel at home in this well-equipped dormitory. The Tianjin YWCA, due to the increasing development of its work, urgently needs to build its own building. This spring, it joined with enthusiastic people from all walks of life to launch a fundraising campaign to build a building, with a goal of 100,000 yuan. Important figures from the Party and the country, as well as famous figures from society, have donated silver cups and shields as awards for those who contribute to the fundraising effort. It is said that about 60,000 yuan has already been raised. Judging from the efforts of the fundraisers and the enthusiastic donations from all walks of life, it should not be difficult to achieve the goal.

Female Lawyer Gu Ruolan Opens Her Practice

Ms. Gu Ruolan graduated from Shanghai College of Law and Political Science and has held important positions in the Jiangsu Provincial Civil Affairs Department, the National Government, the Ministry of Transportation, the Nanjing Special City Party Headquarters, and the Shanghai District Court. She is proficient in law and has extensive experience. She has now started practicing law in Shanghai. Her office is said to be located in the Shanghai Bank Building on Jiangxi Road.
