Local News Two

Actively Proceeding With

The International Club

Mayor Zhang Elected as the First President

Preparatory Committee Elects Seven Members Yesterday

The organization of an International Club was initiated by people from the Chinese and foreign banking and business communities to connect with each other and increase friendship, and it was decided to use the old site of the Greater China Hotel. A preparatory meeting was held at the office of the Yep Kwong Company yesterday afternoon at around 5 p.m. The following are the details:

Resolutions of the International Club

Eighty Chinese and Western figures attended yesterday, all enthusiastically supporting the proposal. The resolution to organize an International Club was unanimously passed as follows: [It is resolved that this meeting supports the proposal to organize an International Club at the Greater China Hotel, and that a charter should be drafted immediately and submitted to the general meeting to be held in September of this year for voting.]

Speech by Mr. Sparke

After the meeting was convened, Mr. Li Fusun proposed that Mr. Sparke, General Manager of Yep Kwong Company, be the chairman. Mr. Sparke's speech was as follows: [The true purpose of today's meeting is to solicit opinions on improving the organization of the International Club, to organize them, and to prepare a charter based on these opinions for submission to the General Meeting for approval. First, it should be explained that the Greater China Syndicate, which acquired the Greater China Hotel, intends to allocate a portion of the land, totaling 23.5 mu, together with the hotel, dance hall, Italian garden, and all its facilities, to the International Club for 1.2 million taels. According to the estimates of Katz & Zeitlin and the opinion of Major Logan, the price demanded is exceptionally low, and its actual value is far more than this. Therefore, the Greater China Syndicate is very generous. The Greater China Syndicate was initiated and organized by seven Chinese and Western comrades, and its purpose is not to make profits, so the value of selling this property to the International Club is very fair. This is what should be stated first. Today's meeting was not convened for fundraising, as the required funds can be raised by issuing 6% bonds, and there is no need to raise additional funds. Mr. Li Shuxiong has sent a letter on this point, and his main points can be endorsed by us, and they will be raised when the financial issue is discussed later. We are almost all familiar with the need for international cooperation. However, empty words are no substitute for facts. This is an effort to organize a large club for people from all countries to meet and to seek practical progress. Shanghai has a prosperous commerce with both Chinese and foreigners. Such an agency is necessary, and the famous Greater China Hotel is the best venue for it. There has been little contact between Chinese and Western people in Shanghai, and there are inevitably various difficulties. The Greater China Hotel has a beautiful environment and a friendly atmosphere. If an International Club is organized there, it will give people from all countries a great opportunity to get to know each other, and Chinese and foreign societies will benefit from it. Important figures on the Chinese side are very sympathetic to this matter, and Mayor Zhang Yuejun has agreed to take the first president's post. This is a good omen for the success of the International Club, so I am happy to report this to you. The International Club has absolutely no political relations, and it is not allowed to be used as a political gathering under any circumstances. After its establishment, its dance hall and Italian garden can be used as a place for members to dine and dance, and its hotel department can be used for members' entertainment, such as playing billiards and mahjong. There are also a number of rooms available for members from other places to stay in Shanghai. This plan can preserve the Greater China Hotel as a place for commemorative social events. In addition to the Greater China Hotel, there is no other suitable place in Shanghai for this purpose. In the future, the committee may lease the club's buildings to others to meet this need, and there may be a small supplement to the revenue, but monthly rentals may not be more than twice a month. In order to avoid lengthy and confusing discussions, the most important points are listed on the agenda for discussion item by item, and I hope that your criticisms are constructive and not destructive. We all know that it is not easy to create such an agency and make it a success, but with so many people attending today and with enthusiastic support, we will be able to achieve the goals we hope for. Finally, there is one more word to say, that the club we are proposing to organize is not in competition with existing clubs or associations, as the Greater China Hotel can attract people mostly for large gatherings and post-meal entertainment. If this club is run successfully, a sports club will be established later, such as horse riding, tennis, polo, etc., which will be favored by young people in general, and young people will get the greatest benefit from this plan. Now, I will invite Mr. Li Fusun and Mr. Begel to speak, and then proceed to discuss the various issues.]

Speech by Li Fusun

Mr. Li Fusun's speech was as follows: The McBain Garden is the most beautiful garden in Shanghai, and the beauty of its construction and flowers and plants is praised by everyone. It was first owned privately, and when the Greater China Hotel was established, it was opened to the public. For several years, Chinese and foreign celebrities have gathered there for all kinds of good events. Last year, the hotel closed down, and the local people thought that the demolition of such a famous garden would be a great loss. Therefore, the Greater China Syndicate was created. The syndicate was initiated by seven Chinese and Western comrades who raised funds to buy the entire McBain Garden. Its purpose was not to make profits but to preserve this beautiful building and to fully open it to society. After a long period of discussion, it was decided to organize an International Club and allocate a portion of the most suitable buildings at the lowest possible price to the International Club to set up a high-class entertainment venue for all people to enjoy the benefits. Ten thousand merchants gather in Shanghai, and the personnel affairs are busy. The focus of our hearts and the words of our mouths are all on business. However, there must be a suitable place for public leisure. Now, with this International Club, Chinese and foreign men and women will be able to take a break from business and relax to wash away the dust and talk to each other to connect their feelings. The buildings, land, and ancillary equipment sold by the syndicate to the club are priced at 1.2 million taels of silver, and according to Katz & Zeitlin's estimate, the total value of the land and buildings is more than 1.64 million taels, and the land alone is worth more than 1.29 million taels, which is enough to prove the huge sacrifice made by the syndicate. The intention of the initiators to maintain public welfare is shared by the public. This matter was jointly planned by Mr. Sparke, Chen Guangfu, and myself, and Mr. Sparke has done his best. The International Club will still be organized by Chinese and Western comrades to purchase the buildings, land, and other equipment. The funds will be the responsibility of the Chinese and Western initiators. The club plans to recruit 200 members, half Chinese and half Western, and 500 as basic members with the right to vote and be elected, and 1,500 as ordinary committee members. The amount of funds will be determined after a certain number have been raised, and a meeting will be held on a regular basis to elect appropriate personnel in an election manner to establish rules and regulations to manage all the measures to achieve perfection. It is planned to invite Mayor Yuejun to serve as the first president of the International Club, with the highest administrative officer of the local government as the leader of the highest and most beautiful club, which is welcomed by the public and will develop in the future. Daily affairs will be handled by one Chinese and one Western clerk. In short, the purpose of organizing the International Club is entirely for the sake of preserving the scenic spots and for the sake of Chinese and foreign reunion. There is absolutely no other purpose.

Mr. White's Speech

Next, Mr. White, the manager of Chen Mao Hang, gave a speech, roughly stating that the Greater China Banking Group's proposal to the International Club was admirable. He believed that the requested price of 1.2 million taels was extremely reasonable. He also said that Mr. Sparke and Mr. Li Ming had launched a very ambitious plan, and that everyone present should fully support and cooperate with them so that the plan could succeed. Following this, Mr. Sparke read out letters from Li Shuxiong, Zhu Boquan, Zhou Zongliang, Qian Xinzhi, Wu Yunzhai, etc., proposing that the initial membership be set at 500, with each member responsible for an initial fee of 500 taels and recruiting one to four new members, so that the million-dollar fund could be easily raised. As for issuing bonds with interest payments, this method seemed inappropriate. After discussion, it was decided to refer this letter, along with the proposer's suggestion to issue 1.4 million taels of bonds, half to be subscribed by Chinese and half by foreigners, to the preparatory committee for review and then to the general meeting for a decision. Regarding membership issues, Mr. Sparke proposed setting the basic membership at 500, with a membership fee of 200 taels, and the ordinary membership at 1,500, with a monthly fee of 15 yuan, payable in advance every six months. Women can only be ordinary members. All affairs of the club and the election committee, etc., will be managed by the basic committee. There will be no honorary members besides these two types of members. This proposal was decided to be submitted to the preparatory committee for review. Next, it was discussed that the club should have one Chinese and one Western secretary, as well as a first-class ballroom manager. Sparke said that in order for the club to succeed, it should recruit first-class talent. It was resolved to refer this to the preparatory committee for review. Afterwards, Mr. Sparke announced that the International Club had absolutely no political relationship, no partisan flavor, and would never hold any political gatherings.

Mayor Zhang Elected as President

At that time, everyone present was extremely crowded, and they unanimously elected Mayor Zhang as the first president of the International Club. Mr. Sparke proposed that the vice president be elected after the membership quota was met, which was approved by the public. Yesterday, it was also resolved that all payments of the International Club should be made in cash instead of promissory notes to avoid the trouble of collection afterwards. Mr. Li Fuxun said that paying in cash was not difficult for Chinese members. It was then resolved to have membership forms printed. Foreign membership lists can be sent to Jardine Matheson & Co., Mr. Broholm, and Chinese membership lists can be sent to the Central Bank, Mr. Zhu Boquan. A general membership meeting will be convened in September of this year to elect a committee and approve the club's constitution and various rules.

Seven Preparatory Committee Members Elected

The preparatory committee unanimously elected Li Fuxun, Chen Guangfu, Zhu Puquan, White, Bredon, Sparke, and White Lang as the seven members. The preparatory committee will be dissolved after the first general meeting is held. According to Mr. Liu Hongsheng's report, the General Affairs Committee of the United China General Association unanimously approved the proposal to organize the International Club. After the members of the United China General Association and the General Assets Corporation of the United China General Association pass the resolution, it will immediately merge with the International Club, and it is hoped that members of the United China General Association can join uniformly. At that time, Mr. Sparke, on behalf of those present, expressed gratitude for the spirit of friendship of the United China General Association. Finally, Mr. Speelman proposed to thank Mr. Sparke and Mr. Li Fuxun. The meeting adjourned at three o'clock.

Smuggling a Huge Amount of Opium

Leading to a Tragic Incident of Vehicle Inspection and Murder

A Large Amount of Sichuan Opium Arrived by Japanese Ship

Worth Approximately Fifty to Sixty Thousand Gold

Secretly Transported Late at Night with Prior Arrangement

Driver Interrogated, Deceased Autopsied

At 1:36 AM yesterday, the Huishan Police Station received a report from West Constable No. 107 stating that gunshots had been heard at the intersection of Zhaofeng Road and Broadway Road. The police chief ordered Detective Black and Chinese Detective Xu Yongyuan to investigate in detail. It was then discovered that someone was using a truck to secretly transport a large amount of opium. When the Indian constable saw this, he ordered the vehicle to stop. When the driver failed to comply, he fired his gun to stop him. One person was killed on the spot, and another was injured by a bullet. The details of the investigation are recorded below:

No. 16, Hua Ji Road, Yihuo Lane, is the residence of Cai Guiji. Cai is in the transportation business and owns three trucks with license plate numbers 16661, 16728, and 16795. He employs truck drivers such as Du Chaozhuan, who comes from Tongzhou and lives at No. 110.5, Taoyuanfang, North Henan Road. Du has been working for Cai for nearly half a year, earning a monthly salary of 40 yuan. Du usually drives truck No. 16728. At about 10 PM the night before, Du had already returned home to sleep when Xiao Wuzi, Cai Guiji's assistant, arrived at Du's home, saying that he had been ordered by the boss to ask Du to go there immediately as there was something to entrust to him. Du immediately obeyed. When he arrived at Cai's house, Cai asked Du to drive the truck. At that time, truck No. 16661 was already parked on the road with two people on it, instructing Du to drive to the Gonghexiang Wharf at the end of Zhaofeng Road. Upon arriving at the wharf, more than 20 people were unloading 24 sacks from the Japanese merchant ship Guangyaowan. It was discovered that the ship had arrived in Shanghai from Sichuan and was docked at the Gonghexiang Wharf.

The 24 Sacks Were Filled with Sichuan Opium, totaling 2,088 pounds, worth 50,000 to 60,000 gold. They were all loaded onto the truck, intending to transport them elsewhere for sale. A man named Xiao Jinsheng was riding in the front of the truck with Du, instructing him to start the engine and drive forward. These people thought that it was late at night, everything was silent, and no one would know. Moreover, the goods were already on the truck, so there was no chance of failure. However, Indian Constables No. 617 and 644, who were stationed at the intersection of Broadway Road and Zhaofeng Road, had already

Discovered the Secret and Lay in Ambush at the Intersection, intending to arrest the truck when it drove out. At this time, four people resembling hooligans suddenly appeared at the entrance of the lane, responsible for keeping watch. Upon seeing the Indian constables investigating, they knew that the matter had been exposed. A man with a severed left arm took out ten yuan banknotes from his side and offered them to the two Indian constables as a bribe, asking them not to interfere in this matter. The two Indian constables

Accepted the Banknotes and Pretended to Agree. Before long, the truck transporting the goods drove towards them. The Indian constables raised their hands and ordered the truck to stop, but to no avail. At this time, the four people also stepped forward to try to stop the Indian constables from taking action. Indian Constable No. 617, seeing that the situation was critical, unloaded his rifle, loaded it, and pulled the trigger, first firing a shot into the air as a warning. The four people, knowing that the matter had been exposed, turned and fled. However, the truck transporting the goods still refused to stop and sped away. The two Indian constables each fired their rifles

At the Vehicle, Indian Constable No. 617 firing five shots and Indian Constable No. 644 firing two shots. At that time, Xiao Jinsheng was hit by two bullets, one in the abdomen, piercing his back, and the other in his right rib, causing him to fall in the truck.

Blood flowed like a spring. The truck driver, Du Chaozhuan, also sustained a bullet wound in his left hand and a graze to his abdomen. The truck's engine was also damaged and unable to move, so it stopped near Hua Ji Road. After the truck stopped, Du immediately got out of the truck and fled, but he was apprehended by the Indian constables, who were blowing their whistles frantically, with the help of Chinese Constables No. 1848 and 1958. Chinese and Western detectives also arrived after hearing the alarm. When they checked the truck, they saw that Xiao Jinsheng was on his last breath. They quickly sent him to Tongren Hospital, but he

Died upon Arrival. They then transported the body to the autopsy room on Ferron Road. They brought Du, along with the truck and opium, to the Huishan Police Station. Because Du was also injured, he was sent to the hospital for treatment. It was also discovered that the one-armed man's name was Xu Xiaogouzi, a hooligan from the Hongkou area, living at No. 260 Seward Road. Chinese and Western detectives went to Xu's and Cai Guiji's houses to arrest them, but both of them had already fled without a trace. They had no choice but to return to the police station and are currently conducting a strict investigation. At 8:00 AM yesterday, detectives from the police station took the truck driver, Du Chaozhuan, from the hospital and

Escorted Him to Court. First, the police station's acting lawyer, Li Zhishan, rose to give a detailed account of the above situation, stating that the police station was prosecuting the defendant, Du Chaozhuan, for the crime of selling opium under Article 6 of the Opium Suppression Law, requesting that the case be postponed in order to apprehend his accomplices. He then presented a package of opium

And a Bribe of Ten Yuan to the Court. Following this, the Chinese, Western, and Indian constables testified one after another, explaining the situation at the time. When questioned, the defendant, Du

Chaozhuan, testified that he had been driving for Cai Guiji for less than half a year with a monthly salary of 40 yuan. Last night, he had already returned home to sleep when Xiao Wuzi came to call him to drive. When he arrived at the Gonghexiang Wharf, he only saw more than 20 people unloading sacks from the ship and loading them onto the truck. He did not know what was in the sacks and was not allowed to get out of the truck to see. After the loading was completed, the deceased sat with him in the front, and he did not see the people in the back clearly. He asked the deceased where they were going, and the deceased said, "You don't need to ask,

Just Drive." So, he started the engine and drove. Before he had gone a few steps, an Indian constable raised his hand and ordered him to stop. He was about to stop the truck when the deceased slapped him in the face and said, "Do you want your life?" He had no choice but to continue driving forward. When he heard the gunshots, he was terrified and lay down beside the truck, so the deceased drove the truck himself. That is why the Indian constable fired his gun and hit the deceased, and so on. Lawyer Zheng Wenkai then came to court and stated that the defendant

Had Sustained Bullet Wounds That Had Not Yet Healed, requesting that he be sent back to the hospital for treatment. The police station lawyer, Li Zhishan, immediately stood up and stated that the defendant could be sent to the police hospital for treatment and requested that the seized opium and the truck used to commit the crime be confiscated first. Judge Xiao Xiexun reviewed the testimony and ordered that the case be adjourned until the morning of the 24th for further questioning. The opium and truck No. 16661

Page 16

The Truck Was Stored in the Warehouse. By the time the case was examined, it was already past ten o'clock. The constable then took the defendant away and transferred him to the autopsy room. Meanwhile, Prosecutor Guo Wei of the Special Court arrived to examine the body of Xiao Jinsheng, ascending the bench to question the Chinese and Western detectives. Then, a woman named Yu Zhou, claiming to be 60 years old and from Wuxi, testified that the deceased, Yu Jinsheng, was her son, 28 years old, who ran a small restaurant at No. 295 Lao Street, Yuanfang Road,

And Requested to Claim the Body. Judge Guo then instructed, "It has been determined that the deceased, Yu Jinsheng, was shot and killed by an Indian constable. The truck driver, Du Chaozhuan, did not obey orders and has been prosecuted by the police station and should be sent to court for trial. The body of Yu Jinsheng is to be claimed and buried by his mother, Yu Zhou."

Ming Yuan Amusement Park Scheduled to Open

Ming Yuan is scheduled to open on Friday, July 24th. Various amusements in the park are listed as follows: (1) Game Machines: The park has several game machines that have never been seen in Shanghai, such as the Remote Boat, Love Chair, Free Colt, Happy Wheel, etc., all of which have special appeal. (2) Dance Floor: The dance floor is unprecedentedly spacious. There are also two groups of excellent orchestras playing strings and mixed music, with melodious and varied tones. The waltzes, polkas, fox trots, and other tunes played are novel and famous, different from the ordinary. (3) Food and Beverage: There are wine stalls, Japanese incense tea gardens, German beer gardens, Chinese restaurants, and Western restaurants, all of which are fully equipped. (4) Swimming Pool: The pool cost a huge 120,000 yuan to build. The water is clear, and it is exceptionally clean, enough to rival the world's great swimming pools. At the opening, Tianyi Film Company will film a sound film. It is also heard that a women's swimming competition will be held in August to elect Miss Shanghai. The park has now contracted with Tianyi Film Company to film sound films during the competition and election, which is sure to be a grand occasion.

Two Czech Journalists on a Round-the-World Trip Revisit Shanghai

Czech journalists Formanik and Tuka walked around the world, having traveled 40,000 miles to reach Shanghai two years ago. They then went to the Philippines, traveled extensively in Japan, Hawaii, and the United States, and continued for another 30,000 miles. Now they have returned to Shanghai, arriving at the port two days ago on the Hikawa Maru. It is heard that they will now travel to the South Seas Islands for eight or nine months before going to South Africa, preparing to end their wanderings and return home next year. According to reports, the two departed from Prague in May 1928, passing through Romania, Turkey, Syria, Mesopotamia, Persia, India, the Federated Malay States, and Cochin China, arriving in China in the summer of 1929. In March of the following year, they arrived in New York in the United States. Mr. Fok returned home due to illness, leaving Mr. Tu in the United States alone. At the beginning of this year, Mr. Fok recovered from his illness and crossed the ocean to the United States again, then traveled extensively in the southwestern states and took a boat from Seattle to Shanghai. All travel expenses were paid by writing articles for various newspapers in Prague and a Czech newspaper in Chicago, and occasionally supplemented by the proceeds from selling art postcards.

Crackdown on Gambling in Concession Amusement Parks

The Municipal Council's Police Department Strictly Enforces

The Municipal Government received a reply from the Municipal Council yesterday, stating that regarding the issue of gambling in various amusement parks and on the streets, the Police Department has begun investigating and handling the matter. Various gambling games in the amusement parks have been successively stopped. As for the crackdown on gambling on the streets, the Bureau's patrolmen will continue to carry it out at any time. According to Zhu Rongping, the proposer of the proposal to ban gambling stalls in amusement parks, the Shanghai Public Concession Taxpayers Association replied, "Regarding your letter of June 6th regarding the establishment of gambling stalls in amusement parks, the Police Department has taken measures to ban them from being held. We are responding accordingly. Please note, etc."

After the Dissolution of Labor University

Two Youths Attempt to Flee Upon Seeing Patrol Officers

Officials' Credentials Found on Their Persons

Now Sent to Court for Interrogation

After the Jiangwan Labor University was ordered to dissolve, the Fifth Precinct of the Fifth District of the Public Security Bureau was ordered to assist in the execution. Unexpectedly, when two youths saw the patrol officers, they jumped over the bamboo fence and attempted to flee. The patrol officers became suspicious and arrested both youths. A credential belonging to a Tan Dingfen was found on his person, a certificate for Tan Dingfen, Chief of the Communications Section of the Communications Department of the Land, Sea, and Air Headquarters, and a passport. A student ID card No. 492 from the Central Political School was found on a Peng Chenshun. They were taken to the Fifth Precinct of the Fifth District together. According to Tan, he was from Sichuan. This certificate was given to him by a friend, and he had no other intention but to ride the train without having to buy a ticket. He had never seen soldiers before, so he was afraid and ran away after seeing them. Peng claimed to be from Hunan and was indeed a student at the Central School. He came to Labor University to look for a friend and stayed for five days. He was inexplicably arrested by the patrol officers because Labor University was dissolved, so he went outside. It was deemed that the case involved impersonating an official, so it was submitted to the Public Security Bureau and transferred to the local court for interrogation yesterday.

Frenchman's Car

Fatally Hits a Pedestrian and is Peacefully Resolved

Wang A'yu, 40 years old, a local resident living at No. 32, Houmalu, Caojiadu, in the Western District of Shanghai, worked at Shenxin Textile Factory. His wife, Yu, is 42 years old and has two sons. The eldest son, Chang'an, is 18 years old, and the youngest is still young. Wang's old illness relapsed recently. On the 11th of this month, feeling slightly better, he went out on business and was walking near the bridge on the Jisi Feier Road Road when a car No. 2829 driven by a Frenchman named Jia Liyang (translation) sped past. Wang was unable to avoid it in time and was knocked to the ground, injuring his abdomen. He was immediately taken to the hospital for treatment. However, due to his old illness and the severity of his injuries, the treatment was ineffective, and he died the day before yesterday. His wife, Yu, then went to negotiate with the Frenchman (who works at the French Electric Company). The Frenchman paid a condolence payment of 400 yuan and introduced his son, Chang'an, to a certain position. The family was quite satisfied, and the matter was peacefully resolved. The family prepared a coffin and proceeded with the funeral.

Soldier

Smuggling 110,000 Red Pills

Yesterday morning around 7:00 AM, Su, a patrol officer from the Yipinli police station of the Fifth District of the Public Security Bureau in Zhabei Baoshan Road, was leading police officers to inspect passengers at the North Railway Station when he saw a soldier in full uniform carrying a suitcase and a bedding roll, acting suspiciously. The police officers stepped forward to inspect and discovered a large number of red pills, totaling 110,000, hidden in the suitcase and bedding roll. The soldier, along with the drugs, was taken to the Fifth District police station for questioning. The soldier claimed that he was Wu Mingsheng, from Nanhui, serving as a soldier in the 8th Company of the 2nd Battalion of the 2nd Regiment of the Gendarmerie of the Capital Garrison Command. These red pills were being transported to Wuxi, worth approximately 500 to 600 gold at the current price.

Robbery at a Shoe Store on Avenue Edward VII

One Thief Apprehended on the Spot

Chen Minzhong, a local resident, opened the Tianyi Shoe Store at No. 533 Avenue Edward VII. At 9:30 PM last night, three robbers suddenly entered, pretending to buy shoes. They drew out their pistols, intending to start searching. However, an extremely alert shop assistant named Deng Zhengmao saw the robbers enter and tried to slip out the back door to call for help. He was spotted by one of the robbers, who chased him out the back door and grabbed Deng. At that time, many people were sitting in the alleyway to cool off, and they knew it was a robbery, so they blew their whistles together and assisted in the pursuit. The two robbers who remained in the store, seeing that the situation was not good, immediately fled, escaping south along the Xinxiao Bridge Street. As they fled to the iron gate of Xinxiao Street, patrol officers from the French Concession happened to be passing by on patrol. They immediately fired three shots into the air as a warning. As a result, one thief was apprehended, and a loaded pistol was seized. He was taken to the police station, where the police chief questioned him in detail and ordered him to be detained temporarily pending trial in court.

Record of the Trial of the Fang and Hu Kidnappers

Fang the Bandit Once Accused Detective Liang of Stealing Morphine

The Police Station Presented a Distribution List as Evidence

Chen Shifan, a native of Ningbo, was engaged in the construction and construction business. At 9:30 PM on December 19th of last year, he was riding in his own car when he was stopped by four kidnappers on Pingwang Street. Chen was taken away and hidden at No. 330 Ladou Road in the French Concession, where he was held for a ransom of 10,000 yuan. Chen bribed the guards with 5,000 gold to escape. Subsequently, the Chinese and Western detectives of the Old Gate Police Station apprehended the kidnappers, Lu Agen from Yangzhou and Zhou Yuying, a woman from Changshu. They were handed over to the Special District Court for sentencing. Lu was sentenced to death, and Xu was sentenced to 20 years in prison. During the court session, Lu Agen stated that Fang Liansheng and Hu Along were accomplices, but because he did not know their addresses, there was no way to investigate. Later, Fang suddenly used the alias Li Liansheng to accuse Liang Chengyu, a Chinese detective at the Inspector General's Office, of stealing more than 50,000 yuan worth of morphine. The police station filed a lawsuit against Detective Liang, and after the trial, Detective Liang was acquitted. At that time, Detective Liang pointed out that Li Liansheng was Fang Liansheng (nicknamed Xiaoliansheng), who was wanted but not caught. In addition to kidnapping Chen Shifan, he was also involved in the kidnapping of Li Huiqing. The police station detained Fang Liansheng. Subsequently, Hua Jin, the Chinese detective chief of the Hongkou Police Station, and detectives Mao Yiwen, Bao Shuji, Zhang Jinlong, Yang Zhaoqing, Liu Zhaonian, etc., apprehended Hu Along and brought him to the Special District Court for interrogation along with Fang Liansheng. Yesterday morning, Judge Xiao Xiexun held three consecutive preliminary hearings. Police station lawyer Li Zhishan stated that the two defendants, in addition to kidnapping Chen Shifan, also kidnapped Li Huiqing on Guangxi Road at 1:00 PM on February 8th of this year, obtaining a ransom of 2,000 yuan. They had confessed to this at the police station. Lu Agen, who had already been sentenced to death, testified that the two defendants were present during the kidnapping. A distribution list was found in Fang's house at No. 179 South Chengdu Road, stating that Fang received one share and Xu Yuying received one and a half shares. The list was presented as evidence. Chen Shifan then testified that it was raining heavily and it was very dark when he was kidnapped, so he could not identify the faces of the bandits. After arriving at the bandits' den, he bribed the guards with 5,000 yuan to escape. His driver, Shen Changfa, testified that he could not identify the two defendants. Li Huiqing had gone to Shantou and had not arrived. Judge Xiao interrogated the two defendants and ordered them to be remanded in custody for further questioning.

Garment Maker Electrocuted

Last night around 9:00 PM, Lu Jiusheng, a garment maker living across from Taiyuanfang, Zhongxing Road, Zhabei, at the newly opened Changsheng Road intersection, Lu's younger brother, Liansheng (35 years old, local resident), attempted to repair the broken light switch in the living room. He did not turn off the power and was electrocuted and fell to the ground as soon as he touched it. When the family learned of this, they turned off the power, but Liansheng was already breathless and unconscious. They immediately called Baolong Hospital in the Concession for a doctor to come and treat him, but it was ineffective. Jin Ertu, the head of the three wards in that area, heard the news and immediately went to Zhongxing Road to report the matter by letter to the branch office. Police Chief Cheng Jun went to investigate and confirmed the facts and immediately reported it to the Fourth District. Today, he petitioned the Shanghai Local Court for an autopsy.

The Zikawei Observatory's weather forecast for yesterday at 4:30 PM stated that the coastal areas are hot and cloudy. The Yangtze River basin may experience thunderstorms. Letters to the Editor

Yesterday, I read the [Appeal Trial of Drug Trafficking Case] in the local news section of your newspaper on July 16th. The first paragraph contains many factual errors. Upon investigation, the manager of the Jieji Company is the shop owner, Li Zhusan, who is also the husband of Yu Zhenxiang. Mr. Yu Zhenxiang is only an employee of the company, specializing in bookkeeping. How could he go out and carry packages? All external matters are managed by Li alone, and her husband has no right to interfere. On that day, the package was moved from the Changsheng Yarn Shop on Diandang Street to the cargo truck by the company's handyman, Li Hongru. On the way, the detectives suddenly arrested the person and seized the goods, and 42 packets of red pills were found in the package. Unexpectedly, the handyman Li Hongru falsely accused her husband of instructing him to do so. As a result, her husband was arrested and sentenced. The two owners of Changsheng and Jieji fled to avoid the situation, causing her husband to be wrongly implicated. Therefore, he has hired a lawyer to appeal according to the law and request a reversal. This is the true story of the case. Please publish this letter in your newspaper to correct the record. Thank you very much. Respectfully, Yu Yao Shi, July 17th, residing at No. 641 North Chengdu Road.

To the Editor, I have read the news in your newspaper's local news column on July 16th regarding the Health Bureau's intensified epidemic prevention work, and there are several inaccuracies. (1) Cholera outbreaks have occurred in India and other places, but leptomeningitis has not become an epidemic. (2) Regarding the dispatch of personnel to board foreign vessels for inspection before landing, it is planned to be jointly handled with the Harbor Epidemic Prevention Office, and it is not being carried out solely by the Municipal Health Bureau. (3) Mr. Zhong's position is not the head of the bureau's department. I am writing to you specifically to request that you investigate and correct the record. Sincerely, Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau, July 17th, to the Editorial Office of the Shen Bao.

To the Editor, According to my client, Mr. Ni Gongwei, the current general manager and resident manager in Hankou of the Sichuan Road Company, he stated in a letter from Beiping that he had read the news reports in the Shen Bao of July 3rd and July 8th regarding the recent communication from the Sichuan Road Shareholders' United Association, which contained many criticisms of the company that could confuse listeners. Upon investigation, the fellow villagers organized the Sichuan Road Shareholders' United Association, advocating for shareholders to hold meetings on their own and opposing everything. However, they do not realize that holding shareholder meetings requires raising a large sum of money. Even if the funds for the liquidation are stored in a secure bank, there must be a legal person responsible for them, which cannot be arbitrarily executed by a small group of shareholders in any one place. Otherwise, if shareholders in various places act independently, the result will still be a lack of funds for holding meetings and no one responsible, allowing those who borrow and embezzle funds to continue to celebrate having an excuse not to repay. In the past, whenever someone was appointed to handle the liquidation, those who borrowed and embezzled funds would secretly instigate their cronies or incite fellow villagers to obstruct and sabotage under the guise of shareholder groups. Although there are many pure and admirable people in the Sichuan Road Shareholders' United Association organized in Shanghai this time, they may not fully understand the actual situation of the company and the responsibilities that Mr. Ni Gongwei is currently bearing. Mr. Ni Gongwei was elected and appointed as the general manager and resident manager in Hankou with the consent of the majority of directors in the form of letters and telegrams, entrusted with the responsibility of holding meetings and liquidation. He also obtained the approval of the provincial government and dispatched Mr. Wang Zhai Shi to supervise the liquidation and prepare for the meeting. Since taking office, the company has not had a single fund to work with and has been running around borrowing money, tirelessly enduring complaints. He has accumulated and liquidated assets in Shanghai, Hankou, Pingjin, and other places to protect the company's rights. He has also submitted a request to the provincial government to approve the holding of a shareholders' meeting at the company's headquarters on October 21st of this year. He believes that his humble talents bear this important responsibility. He would be grateful if the majority of pure gentlemen in the Shareholders' United Association could provide legitimate guidance. Even if there are derelictions of duty, they can be questioned or sued according to the law. However, he does not want them to be used by others without knowing the inside story, making baseless accusations that harm his personal reputation and obstruct the liquidation and meeting affairs. Therefore, I respectfully request that you forward this letter to the Shen Xin and other newspapers to be disclosed in the "Letters to the Editor" column as a correction. Sincerely, Lawyer Yu Zhongluo, July 17th, to the Shen Bao.

Free Talk

A Few Words

— Zhang Xiafei

Most women demand material things more than spiritual comfort.

The modern girl's heart is like a floating cloud in the sky, drifting there.

Opening a salted egg and slowly digging it out to eat is more flavorful than slicing it. Love is also like that.

Love changes from the shape of the heart, so the danger of love often arises from a change of heart.

The objects of love are regret, depression, hatred, depravity, suicide, etc...

Modern girls cherish their looks more than fishermen cherish their fishing hooks.

It is better to live alone in peace than to live with someone of the opposite sex with whom you are incompatible.

When you buy a book, you should read it, not just use it as a decoration on the bookshelf.

Use your ears more and your mouth less, that is the way for young people to deal with the world.

When we do things, our hearts should be hot, but our minds should be cold.

People have four parts intelligence, but they need two parts honesty.

Study Abroad in Ceylon

— Huang Maolin

I have been planning to study in Ceylon for several years. Last winter, I decided to go, and after three or four months of preparation and the support of various virtuous people, I was able to fulfill my wish and set sail on the 3rd of February of the 20th year, taking the Kashima Maru to Hong Kong. I arrived in Hong Kong after seven days and went home to visit my family, from whom I had been separated for eleven years. That evening, the ship went to Singapore, where the Buddhist Research Association had a beautiful new Buddhist hall with six Buddha statues made of marble from Italy, each worth about 4,000 Chinese silver dollars, which was very solemn. On the afternoon of the 18th, I arrived in Colombo, the capital of Ceylon. The Buddhist School sent a Sanskrit professor, Mr. Batte, to pick me up. Mr. Batte is a high-ranking Brahmin who has recently converted to Buddhism, a dignified scholar. The Maha Bodhi Society of this place also sent someone to the ship to welcome me with great enthusiasm. He had studied in the East and was an enthusiastic Buddhist. He had translated my [Overseas Buddhist News] published in the third issue of an English magazine into the local language and published it in the newspaper. After I landed, I went to the Buddhist School to visit the elder, who is proficient in Pali and Sanskrit and is famous for his morality and learning in this land, a kind and benevolent person. The school is located four or five miles from the city and has beautiful scenery. There are about 20 people living and studying here, including Indian monks and Nepalese monks. There are also laymen and monks who give lectures, dozens of people. The school is translated as [Mingzhen], the word [Ming] means [learning], such as [Five Ming Treasures] or [Solemn], the translated meaning is [Treasure of the School]. This school is one of the famous Buddhist colleges in this land with a long history. The previous governor of Ceylon, Mr. Zhan Ma, came here every day to study Pali and translated the English Madhyama Agama Sutra. After I met the elder, I went to the Buddhist hall to worship the Buddha. In this place, one cannot wear shoes or socks when worshiping the Buddha. The candles burned are white western candles, and the offerings are flowers. Incense may or may not be burned. The method of worship is different from that in China. One must walk around the pagoda three times and worship the Bodhi tree, walking around the tree three times. This is the usual practice of worshiping the Buddha.

Each temple has a pagoda and a tree. Before worshiping the Buddha and walking around, one must wash their face and be barefoot. Here, one gets up at 6:00 AM every day, takes a cold shower, and then worships the Buddha at 7:00 AM. At 8:00 AM, one has breakfast of white rice and curry. Classes start at 9:00 AM and lunch is at 11:30 AM, consisting of rice, curry, and vegetables. At 7:00 PM, one worships the Buddha, chants scriptures, and then prostrates to the elder to repent of the actions of the body, mouth, and mind of the day. The elder replies, [I am also like that.] Here, monks are highly respected, and it is taken very seriously. Laypeople cannot sit on an equal footing with monks. One does not return the prostration of monks. The diligence of the monks is also admirable and amazing. The Nepalese monk in the next room knows several languages, including English and Tibetan. He gets up at 5:00 AM every day and immediately reads the scriptures. The sound of his reading can still be heard at 10:00 PM. The Sanskrit professor teaches every day and studies German and French on his own. He will soon take the doctoral exam at a certain German university. His diligence is very rare. The chairman of this school is the Deputy Speaker of the Ceylon Parliament, who is proficient in Theravada Buddhism and has a master's degree in liberal arts from England, a charitable gentleman. Knowing that I had come here, he sent a letter from Shanghai welcoming me to study here. Unfortunately, when the letter arrived, I had already left Shanghai. On the night of February 19th, he personally came to the school to visit me, but I was staying at the Buddhist Youth Association because of some matters. He is the president of the Youth Association and visited me late at night, inviting me to have lunch at his house on Sunday. The expenses for my stay at the Youth Association for a few days were also paid by him, which is very touching.

On February 23rd, I took a car to Kandy to pay homage to the Buddha's tooth and visit several ancient temples, all guided by Mr. On March 1st, I returned to school. On March 5th, I started Pali class, and on the 7th, I started Sanskrit class. Here, the morning and evening classes are all in Pali and must be memorized. In addition, Sanskrit and Pali are very complex, especially difficult for beginners. Therefore, I cannot take care of Chinese translation and editing magazines until three or four months later.

The Incomparable Courage of a Ten-Year-Old

— Yi

After reading the article about the young girl who defeated the thieves and recovered everything (see the 10th issue of this publication), no one can help but admire the girl's extraordinary wisdom. Unexpectedly, another similar event occurred. Someone from Taizhou came to Shanghai and told me about a ten-year-old boy who defeated the thieves and recovered everything. She was a female, and this is a male. She used wisdom, and this one used courage, which is even more admirable. The fact that it happened in Taizhou makes it even more worthwhile to promote. The young boy's surname is Zhang. His family lives more than twenty miles from the city. His father is originally a tenant farmer, but he is quite wealthy because he has been diligent and frugal all his life, and he treats money as his life. Therefore, he has accumulated savings and become a well-off family. In recent years, Taizhou has also suffered from many thieves, and murders and robberies occur from time to time. The villages have all raised funds to defend themselves. When there is an alarm, they beat gongs to gather the people to resist the thieves, and the situation has improved slightly compared to before. One night, Mr. Zhang was chatting with his family when suddenly more than a dozen thieves broke into the house, each holding a handgun and flashlight, raging like a pack of tigers and wolves. Mr. Zhang did not have time to hide and was captured by the thieves, who tied his hands and pointed a handgun at his chest, forbidding him to make a sound. They did the same to Mrs. Zhang. Both husband and wife were terrified and looked like no one. The thieves then opened boxes and overturned chests, searching and looting wildly. They divided into groups and robbed neighboring households. In the end, only two thieves remained in Zhang's house, still searching and rummaging. When the thieves first entered the house and tied up Mr. and Mrs. Zhang, the young boy hid in the corner of the room and gradually crawled under the table. The thieves shone a flashlight on him and saw that he was a child and did not pay attention to him. The boy also kept silent. By this time, the thieves had almost forgotten about the boy under the table. The boy saw that there were only two thieves left. He quietly went to the corner of the room and took a door bolt. Taking advantage of the thieves crouching and searching and rummaging, he suddenly raised the bolt and slammed it hard on the head of one of the thieves. The thief was caught off guard and immediately fell to the ground. Another thief heard the noise and looked around in shock. The boy continued to raise the door bolt and struck him with force. Although he hit the thief's shoulder, he was not seriously injured. The thief angrily wanted to grab him, but the boy had already run out of the house. The thief chased after him but could not catch him. Soon after, they heard the loud sound of gongs being beaten. The villagers rushed to gather and shout, and the sound shook several miles. The two thieves in Zhang's house abandoned all the stolen goods and fled. The thief who had been hit on the head was still in terrible pain. At the same time, the thieves who were robbing neighboring houses were also panicked and only cared about escaping, not daring to take the stolen goods with them. The fact that the robbed households did not suffer any losses was all due to the efforts of the young boy alone. When he escaped from his house, he went to a house with a gong and obtained one. He beat it wildly to call for help. When the villagers heard the sound of the gong, hundreds of people gathered unexpectedly. Everyone was afraid that the thieves had weapons, so they shouted in unison to intimidate them. The thieves were indeed frightened and ran away, not being able to capture a single person.

A Funeral Couplet for the Late Major General Hu Deru, Commander of the 5th Army

— Xu Ganxia

Fighting for the revolution, sacrificing for the hometown, his great deeds shine forever, and his heroic name will be passed down for eternity.

He is a pillar of the party and the country, a model soldier, his merits are long-standing, and his life's work is worthy of a thousand autumns.

Brief News It is noted that since the prevalence of sound films, major cinemas in Shanghai have changed to showing sound films. Only the Paris Cinema on Avenue Joffre shows silent films, but the cinema also changed to sound films a month ago, leading to the disappointment of silent drama fans in Shanghai. The cinema is now showing silent films again (besides sound films, two silent works will be selected to show every month). The first silent film to be shown is a latest production from Germany, [Human Desire], a story about a young couple who goes astray, causing various bad consequences. The film shows the bad things couples can do, intending to promote morality. The dramatic plot and moving expressions is able to capture the heart and provide education as entertainment. The film will start showing on Friday.

Rambles in Korea (8)

— Ji Ping

The history of Chinese people living in the Korean Peninsula is long. The establishment of the Four Commanderies of Lelang, Imdun, Hyeondo, and Jinbeon by Zhou Feng Jizi in Korea during the Han Dynasty is sufficient to prove it. Geographically, Incheon in Korea is only separated from Shandong by a body of water, making transportation very convenient. Therefore, there are more Shandong people in Korea than people from other provinces. According to the latest survey, the total number of overseas Chinese is nearly 100,000, generally divided into three types of occupations: agriculture, industry, and commerce. Although they have lower knowledge, their virtues of diligence and hard work exceed those of the Japanese and Koreans. But for this reason, they are often envied and excluded by the Japanese and Koreans, and the voices of排斥華僑 are getting louder.

Whether Chinese businessmen in Korea are local merchants or urban merchants, when they start their businesses, they must reserve a portion of their property outside of the commercial capital. Sometimes, when the market is panicked or there is an unexpected loss, their lives will not be suddenly affected. At the beginning of their operations, they are often in small, remote alleys with small storefronts, and all transactions, such as bread, cotton cloth, groceries, and food, have been established for many years. Before long, a grand Chinese-style store is established. This is a common occurrence. The steps of their commercial development are from small to large, from near to far. On the basis of doing business, they are indeed more stable than Japanese and Korean businessmen. Otherwise, how can they survive in such an evil environment?

The number of overseas Chinese engaged in agriculture in the whole of Korea is estimated to be more than 14,000, mostly living in the suburbs of major cities. The most important thing for urban people every day is vegetables, and overseas Chinese farmers supply them as much as they need, which is their only way of life. In recent years, with the immigration of Japanese, the addition of railways, and the development of industry and commerce, Korean cities have seen a large concentration of population, and the demand for vegetables has increased day by day. The productivity of overseas Chinese farmers has also continued to grow. They are all strong and energetic, and their spirit of labor is by no means comparable to that of the Japanese and Korean people. They work in the fields, working at sunrise and resting at sunset, and the quality of the vegetables they grow is excellent. Even in Seoul, Incheon, and Pyongyang, most of the vegetable market is occupied by overseas Chinese farmers. In addition, they also use their spare time to engage in the sideline of raising pigs, sheep, chickens, and ducks. Unfortunately, they have not received education, have little knowledge, and are easily deceived, especially by the Japanese.

The number of overseas Chinese workers in Korea is more than 30,000, including road construction workers, stone workers, carpenters, miners, sculptors, porters, barbers, and blacksmiths. They all have autonomous groups, which are so-called [gangs]. The main reason for their organization is the relationship between fellow villagers or the relationship between fellow workers. Although their language habits, knowledge, and skills are different, they are able to gain a foothold in Korea thanks to the [gang]. They mostly appoint one person as [leader], and under his command, dozens or hundreds of people are gathered to form an organization of a certain [gang]. After overseas Chinese workers join a [gang], not only must they obey the [leader]'s orders, but they must also strictly abide by the gang rules, and they cannot engage in the work of other gangs. The leader can represent the entire [gang] and conclude contracts with entrepreneurs or entrepreneurs' groups, so that the [gang] often has a monopoly victory. The result of their group training is that no one is not diligent and no one is not working hard, so they can excel over others. The reason is that overseas Chinese workers are able to work hard, are obedient, and can obtain the highest efficiency at the lowest cost, so entrepreneurs attach great importance to them. Some of the Japanese and Koreans are very jealous, while others want to take advantage of them, creating a contradictory phenomenon.

Rotary Club Storytelling

？？？ (25)

— Xu Zhuodai

[To the left!]

Mrs. dislikes monotony the most. Seeing her husband stroke her by her side, she would order him to turn left. Sometimes she wants to walk alternately to the left and right, sometimes she wants to walk in a straight line, sometimes she wants to walk in a circle, sometimes she must walk in an ellipse. There are also times she requires her husband to count one, two, three, four, like doing gymnastics. There are also times when she is annoyed by calling the numbers too simple, and she wants Ziliang to sing a song [The Poor Autumn Fragrance]. In short, the changes are endless and must be ordered by her temporarily.

Suddenly, the wife, whose liver was hurting, laughed loudly.

[Ticklish.]

She covered her chest with both hands and would not allow Ziliang to stroke her again and kept laughing. Ziliang stopped his hands, not knowing what was going on.

[Don't let you use your hands anymore!]

[Are you alright?]

Ziliang asked cautiously. The wife did not speak and continued to laugh wildly. Suddenly, she sat up.

[Thank you! Pour me a cup of tea to drink!]

[Is the liver pain better?]

Mrs. nodded. Ziliang went downstairs to pour a cup of hot tea and brought it to the front of the bed, seeing that his wife had already lain down again.

[The tea is here, get up and drink!]

[I don't want to drink!]

Ziliang felt very surprised.

[Are you feeling unwell again?]

[No!]

[If you don't want to drink tea, why did you ask me to pour it?]

Mrs. suddenly laughed again.

[This cup of tea is my treat for you!]

[Why?]

[You worked hard just now, so I'm treating you to a cup of tea!]

New Gate Yesterday, a total of twenty-four and five goods arrived on West Road. The Changxi and Erbang trades in this street are the best. Early and late rice guest gangs have a slight activity. The market improved. The Kunshan, Jiangyin, and other thick japonica rice sales are also not bad. The price per dan continues to be five cents lower. The price of Luyang tip rice is no up or down. The supply of Port Tip River is scarce. Only two tubes were sold in the same number of dans on that day. The momentum picked up by several points. The appetite for glutinous rice is scarce, presenting a downstream image. The river down dan feet are about two or three thousand dan.

South City The amount of road source is not much. Both urban and rural stores are easy to stay due to inventory, so select fresh material and slightly take the stomach. Those who stay are rarely inquired. The sale shows this image. Staying goods seem difficult to be determined, and they are all loose. Fresh and violent goods are tight due to lack, so the attitude of thick japonica rice is high and secondary soft, returning to the spinning state. Thin rice has not accumulated much. Both the 宁胃 appetite and the street sales are fresh and high. The market situation of medium and secondary rice is flat and steady. The arrival of Luyang tip is not much, and the appetite is also slack. The decline is due to the cheap price of white yuan, and the sale is more dull, so the price of fresh goods is temporarily determined. The arrival of Western rice is still lacking. There are only sporadic transactions in this street. The market shape is fixed and firm.

Flour Tianjin Gang Actively Drawing and Loading

Yesterday, the flour market presented a near-stable and far-flat image. The reason for this is that the Tianjin area has seen a smooth spot sales in recent days, about 70,000 or 80,000. It is heard that a large batch of sales are 共軍 grain, so those who draw and load in the Tianjin gang are quite active. Fuxin also helps the prosperity of the guest gang and has also received advances, causing this month to step open and step firm. For expired months, the mills have hedgeouts, and buyers are not very brave, so the market is in a stable situation. Observing the later steps will be a spinning image, not too high a hope. As a result, this month is 7 mils better than the previous day, August is 5 mils better, September is 2 mils and a half better, October is 2 mils smaller, November did not move, and December is 5 mils smaller cloud.

Spot Wheat Still Clogged

Standards Should Be Lower

Yesterday, the wheat market presented a flat and tired trend. Although the quoted price of 洋麦 foreign wheat rose back by 5 cents, most people's hearts are still difficult to shake because spot wheat is still clogged. Not only the inventory in this port cannot be sold through, but the inventory in other ports has become more and more overflowing since the new one was produced. The middle mills are all not moving. In this situation, people's hearts naturally feel uneasy, and those who throw goods at the standard feel that there are many people. Each mill is gradually declining due to poor morale. As a result, this month is 3 cents smaller than the previous day, August and September are 3 cents smaller, October is 1 cent smaller, November is 1 cent larger, and December did not move. The spot wheat market is still stable. The whole market opened with Yangzhou, Zhenjiang, Nanjing, Dongtai, Chuzhou, and other more than 20 kinds of wheat. Fuxin handled 2,600 bales, Huafeng handled 1,400 bales, and Xiangxing handled 300 bales, it is said.

Silk and Tea

European and American Silk Sales Lonely and Without Spirit

European and American markets are stagnant due to the German economic panic. Silk mills are not selling. Shanghai port electricity is not transferring. Yesterday, only Boxing advanced 6 packages of yellow silk and Xinfu advanced 5 packages of white silk. Meida advanced 10 packages of yellow rough silk. The prices are all flat and tired cloud.

Needle-Eyebrow Green Tea French Sales Continue Smoothly

Yesterday, the Zhenmei green tea from Wuyuan and Tunxi and other roads in the Foreign firm tea market of this port, all started to handle business in 協新·同孚·福時·永興 and other firms. The market continued to trend smoothly, but the selling price fell by more than ten taels. The highest market price of Wuyuan Eastern 鄕貢熙茶 opened by 富林 Foreign Firm yesterday was 120 taels, which is the highest price in recent years, but the situation of ordinary goods is still difficult to be optimistic because the money shop has not yet opened. The Zhenmei market is still depressed. Transactions of upper and middle firm goods are scarce. Although the low-firm goods in Wenzhou and Yushan and other roads have a removal stomach, the inventory is no longer visible.

Social News

East-West Reflections

— Zhen

Dr. Xie Shou Kang, the Chargé d'Affaires to Belgium, has a new book [East-West Reflections], most of which are lectures given by the doctor in Europe. It will be published soon. The foreword by the Belgian Foreign Minister Simon is as follows:

Since the indirect communication between China, Free Asia, and the former part (i.e. Turkey and Persia) and Rome, the West has always been surprised and admired. At the beginning of the 17th century, Marco Polo's records of Genghis Khan's guests aroused endless fantasies. Later, Columbus sailed across the Atlantic Ocean and mistakenly thought he was sailing to the east coast of Asia, and regarded Cuba as Cathay. As soon as he landed, he wrote to Genghis Khan. In the 18th century, the Westerner's love for exotism Exatisme changed the trend. Chinese exquisite magnetic strange lacquerware was widely sought after, and the decoration of the living room was also painted with Chinese figures and landscapes. Since then, the long history of the Chinese empire, the legacy of thousands of years, the ancient Shangde literature and art have been systematically studied, and the sudden changes in modern China have increased our interest and meaning. Therefore, we are delighted to welcome any works that can facilitate this still mysterious world. We are especially grateful to Dr. Xie Shou Kang, Dean of the Faculty of Arts of Nanjing Central University and Chargé d'Affaires of China to Belgium, for printing his speeches such as [China Ancient and Modern]. You graduated from the Paris School of Political Science and the Department of Sociology of Lausanne University with a Bachelor's degree, and a Doctor of Economics from Beijing University. You are well versed in Western literature and are a famous author of French tragedies. Your play [Sui Yu] was performed at the Royal Theatre in Belgium and achieved great success for a while. Mr. Xie's ability to make excellent Chinese elements communicate with the European intellectual circles is particularly appropriate. Mr. Xie is knowledgeable and connected politics through literature, so he is not only a politician and diplomat, but also a writer and scientist. Mr. Xie is able to realize his thoughts and actions equally, not as a poet who is angry with the world, but [as a non-dream sister in a world]. The materials in this book are completely contrary to other empty clichés and speeches without data. The text is concise and everywhere. See the truth. The topic begins with a general idea and then folds into details, and even the most subtle understanding. Under the pen of this learned master, reading the long history of China from the ancient emperor who invented medicine, architecture, and calligraphy to the pioneer Sun Yat-sen who strived to reform and create a new China, I feel happy and refreshed. Sun Yat-sen, in view of the past situation and to supplement the modern Anglo-Saxon constitution, adopted the oldest organization of the empire. In the past, the Chinese Censorate could punish officials, accuse high officials, and directly report to the emperor at any time. In addition, Chinese official positions were determined according to examination results. Therefore, Sun Yat-sen adopted our three powers of the civil system and added two inherent Chinese powers, namely the power of supervision and the power of examination. Mr. Xie stated that the five-power constitution of the Republic of China is the administration, legislation, justice, supervision, and examination. Simply put, this is nothing more than an allocation mechanism on the powers of Europe and the United States. Although the institutions are different, they are all subordinate to the national government. For example, the members of the Legislative Yuan, the Examination Yuan, and the Supervisory Yuan are all appointed by the government. The work of this complex institution and the reform of a part of the current experience are enough for our detailed investigation. Mr. Xie also clearly explained Confucius' doctrine, which created China as a family with the emperor as the parent for centuries. After talking about calligraphy and literature, he briefly described the slow reform of Chinese literature until the restoration movement of this century. He detailed the history of the Liyuan opera school, which was founded in the Tang Dynasty in 720 AD, and the communication between modern national opera and European opera, which is more meaningful. This book also contains his speech on [Reflections on the Centennial Anniversary of Belgium], which proves his knowledge and understanding of Belgium, which is rare even in my slightly different neighboring country, and his admiration for Belgium is especially sincere. Therefore, in addition to admiring Dr. Xie's intelligence and knowledge, we also have sincere friendship. Dr. Xie's book helps us understand the concept of a very large nation that is now engaged in restoration. We deeply love the treasure house of its ancient culture and wish the future of this new republic is limitless. Here, we deeply know that the desire of the new China is to abolish the obstacles of the past 100 years and enjoy complete sovereignty like other countries. Looking back at the facts, it is enough to prove the goodwill between our two governments. The preliminary treaty of November 22, 1928 (to replace the treaty of 1865) announced that Western tariffs are equal to Belgian justice and recognized in principle the abandonment of consular jurisdiction. The contract on the remaining debt of the Gengzi Indemnity in 1927 used most of the funds for charitable causes and Sino-Belgian education. The agreement of August 31, 1929, for the implementation of this agreement, the Belgian concession in Tianjin was handed over to the Chinese authorities for takeover on January 15, 1931. An author who reveals the clear outline of his country and his fair opinions, and who possesses diplomatic art and literature, is not only beneficial to the ideological circles, but also to international harmony.

Mongolia's Commerce

— You Chen

Since the Mongolian Conference was held in Nanjing, many concrete proposals have been made for the construction of a new Mongolia with the Three People's Principles. Among them, there are detailed plans for transportation construction and industrial development. Now, a general description of the current state of Mongolian commerce is given.

Mongolia is a plateau with overlapping mountains located in the abdomen of Asia. Its area is roughly equivalent to the eighteen provinces of mainland China, but the population density is extremely sparse, with a total of no more than three million people. Mongolia is rich in natural products and is suitable for animal husbandry. Therefore, nineteen out of ten people are engaged in animal husbandry, and it is famous for producing various excellent furs. Most of the furs produced are transported to the United States, and the United States also exports various industrial manufactured products, such as car manufacturing, sugar, leather, etc. to Mongolia in exchange.

After the Revolution of 1911, there was turmoil in the country, and Mongolia took the opportunity to declare independence and build the so-called [Mongolian National Government]. Influenced by Soviet Russia, it was decided that all commerce must be absolutely managed by the government, and it was announced that there would be no restrictions, and all profits would belong to the people. Therefore, the government specially established a cooperative purchasing organization. All commodities imported into Mongolia without passing through this organization would not be protected by the government. In addition, all independent or privately operated imports must be taxed, and the price is also estimated by the cooperative organization. The Mongolian government mostly purchases goods directly, or the general machinery of the Mongolian Cooperative in Kulun handles the business. The cooperative purchasing staff are stationed in various countries, including Moscow, Harbin, and Tianjin as the three major branches. The distribution offices of Mongolian native products are stationed in Leipzig, Germany, and New York, USA.

It is found that there are two channels for Mongolia's trade. One passes through Zhangjiakou, the commercial center in the south, to Tianjin and the sea port. The other passes through Kulun, the center of Mongolia, to Soviet Russia, and from the Northwest Siberian Railway to Haishenwai sea port. In peacetime, it mostly goes from Kulun to the trade centers of Manchuria and Hailar, and then via the Middle East Railway to Harbin. From Mongolia to Soviet Russia, cars, camels, ox carts, merchant caravans, ships, and airplanes are mostly used to transport goods. Those from Zhangjiakou in the south only use cars. The north route can be tax-free, and the transportation cost is also lighter than the south route. The journey is also more stable than the south route. Because the south route has to pay more tariff taxes, and the journey is restless, with many bandits. When the goods are transported to Zhangjiakou, they are transported by train to Tianjin. Due to the extra tax and unsafe roads, merchants have no profit even if they raise the price. The north route transportation mostly uses cars or waterways in summer, and camels in winter. As for air passenger transport, it runs every two weeks throughout the year.

During the Sino-Russian War in the autumn of 1929, due to military relations on the Middle East Road, Mongolia's fur trade in Manchuria and Hailar suffered greatly. The southern transportation took the opportunity to be smooth, and Zhangjiakou also restored its status as a fur center. Zhangjiakou was originally an important commercial market inside and outside Mongolia. Since the Mongolian government established the central procurement agency, and because of the heavy taxes and protection fees, the southern commerce declined sharply and shifted to the north route to enter the sphere of influence of Soviet Russia.

The goods transported from Kulun to Haishenwai are mostly furs. The sales of this fur are mostly in the United States. At the same time, Mongolia's imports are mostly Russian gasoline and oils, European groceries, and German machinery. Although some of the industrial products shipped from the United States to Mongolia recently entered Mongolia from Manchuria and Hailar, most of them still take the road of Zhangjiakou.

The industrial products shipped from the United States to Mongolia are mainly cargo trucks and private cars ranging from half a ton to one and a half tons. Regardless of the size of the car body, cargo transport or passenger transport is extremely crowded. After the cars arrive in Mongolia, the car bodies are mostly modified to facilitate cargo transport. A car that can accommodate seven passengers often seats up to twenty-five people, plus luggage, etc., for weeks-long trips. In addition, the United States also ships minerals, candies, wheat flour, and leather to Mongolia. According to statistics in 1936, there were more than 500 boxes of California-produced sugar transported from Tianjin to Kulun. The number of those transported from Harbin was also large. Leather is a raw material that is made into boots and shoes in Harbin and then imported into Mongolia, where the market is extremely large.

From the above, Mongolia is indeed an excellent place with natural resources. Unfortunately, the transportation with mainland China is obstructed, making commerce unable to prosper. Especially, the immature idea of the government managing commerce due to the Soviet Russian instigation of the Mongolian government is the hidden worry of Mongolian commerce. Due to the inconvenience of transportation, the domestic goods of mainland China cannot be transported to supply its needs, causing Manchuria and Mongolia to become the war tails of imperialism's surplus industrial products. This is extremely urgent to save.

Explorer Ameng Zeng is Said to be Alive

Russian Icebreaker to Explore the Arctic This Summer

Moscow News: The rumor that explorer Ameng Zeng is alive in the Arctic is quite shocking. It is reported that Russia has decided to send the icebreaker Maiyijin to the Arctic for exploration this summer. Nobire also plans to participate in the trip.

Japan's Unemployed in March are Approximately 400,000

Presenting the Highest Record at the End of September of the Previous Year

According to the survey by the Social Affairs Bureau of the Japanese Ministry of Internal Affairs, the estimated number of unemployed persons in the country in March of this year was 396,828, presenting the highest record since September of the previous year, an increase of 45,239 from March of last year and an increase of 9,368 from February of this year. The unemployment rate was 5.79, an increase of 0.8 from March of last year and an increase of 0.18 from February of this year.

The Ethnicity of Childless Divorcees

The United States is Moving Towards This Path

Lewis, Secretary of the American Childhood Alliance, published an article in America's oldest religious publication [Churchman], saying that the United States will become a [nation of childless divorcees] and is moving towards this path. At present, the divorce rate in the United States is increasing daily, while the birth rate is falling daily. As a result, there are very few families in the country. This is a terrible phenomenon. In 1880, the ratio of children under the age of 15 to the national population was 38%, but it fell to 32% last year. The current birth rate is only half of what it was 50 years ago. Compared with 1880, the United States has lost almost 5 million children based on the rate in 1930. The reasons include new ideas, new living standards, and birth control methods, all of which are related to it. The delayed age of marriage is also a factor. Not long ago, women who were not married by the age of 21 sighed as [old maids]. Now it is not the case. They often marry at the age of 24 or 25, and there are even older ones.

The International Geographical Congress will be Held in Paris

The Japanese Side Takes the Opportunity to Open a Exhibition on Human Geography

Paris News: The International Geographical Congress is scheduled to be held in Paris in mid-September of this year. The Japanese side plans to take the opportunity to open a exhibition on human geography to display Japan's population distribution map, the changes in villages, cities, walls, temples, shrines, etc., aerial photographs, and other ancient fifty-three times of scrolls, etc., in order to show the development of Japanese studies.

China's Cotton Exports to Japan Decreased

Approximately 200,000 Bales Reduced This Session

According to the survey by the Japan Cotton Traders Association, the total amount of cotton imported to Japan from various countries from September of last year to the end of June of this year was 3,076,503 bales of Chinese, Indian, American, Egyptian, and other cottons. The same period last year was 2,871,127 bales. Among them, Chinese cotton this session was 434,587 bales, and the previous session was 454,436 bales.

Social News Submission Guidelines

(1) The text should be about domestic and foreign science, industry, commerce, agriculture

(2) News about hygiene, aviation, exploration, customs, or urban life is limited to lyrical paintings about social life.

(3) Photos of seasons, landscapes, animals, plants, people, and news photography are qualified. Female photos in seasonal landscape photography are especially welcome.

(4) Each article should not exceed 2,000 words.

(5) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(6) Do not write the manuscript horizontally. Do not write the words carelessly. Western texts can be omitted as much as possible. If it is necessary to quote the original text, it must be attached to the translation.

(7) Do not use blue ink for drawing and do not use colored paper. White paper and black drawings must be used.

(8) Please indicate that the manuscript is to be received by the Social News Editorial Department.

(9) Whether or not the manuscript is published will not be returned. If it needs to be returned, it should be stated in advance and sufficient postage should be attached.

(10) Remuneration for text is three yuan, two yuan, and one yuan per thousand words in three categories. Photos and special features are paid separately for each picture according to the same example.
